The author acknowledges financial support from the Hong Kong Research Grants Council (GRF Grant No. 15218825) and The Hong Kong Polytechnic University (Grant No. P0045668). ‚ÄÉXiaonyu Xia333College of Mathematics and Physics, Wenzhou University, Wenzhou 325035, China; email: xiaonyu.xia@wzu.edu.cn. ###### Abstract

We study an optimal control problem on infinite time horizon with semimartingale strategies, random coefficients and regime switching. The value function and the optimal strategy can be characterized in terms of three systems of backward stochastic differential equations (BSDEs) with infinite horizon. One of them is a system of linear BSDEs with unbounded coefficients and infinite horizon, which seems to be new in literature. We establish the existence of the solutions to these BSDEs by BMO analysis and comparison theorem for multi-dimensional BSDEs. Next, we establish that the optimal control problem is well posed, in the sense that the value function is finite and the optimal strategy‚ÄĒwhen it exists‚ÄĒis unique. This is achieved by reformulating the cost functional as the sum of a quadratic functional and the candidate value function. The reformulation crucially relies on the well‚ÄĎestablished well‚ÄĎposedness results for systems of BSDEs. Finally, under additional assumptions, we obtain the unique optimal strategy.

AMS Subject Classification: 93E20, 91B70, 60H30

Keywords: infinite-horizon stochastic control, system of BSDEs with stochastic Lipschitz driver, regime switching, semimartingale strategy

## 1 Introduction

Let (ő©,‚ĄĪ,‚Ąô)(\Omega,\mathcal{F},\mathbb{P}) be a fixed complete probability space on which we define a Brownian motion WW and a continuous-time stationary Markov chain őĪ\alpha valued in a finite state space ‚Ą≥={1,2,‚Ä¶,‚Ąď}\mathcal{M}=\left\{1,2,\dots,\ell\right\} with ‚Ąď‚Č•1\ell\geq 1. The Markov chain has a generator matrix (qi‚Äčj)‚Ąď√ó‚Ąď(q^{ij})\_{\ell\times\ell} with qi‚Äčj‚Č•0q^{ij}\geq 0 for i‚Č†ji\neq j and ‚ąĎj=1‚Ąďqi‚Äčj=0\sum^{\ell}\_{j=1}q^{ij}=0 for each i‚ąą‚Ą≥i\in\cal M.
We assume WW and őĪ\alpha are independent of each other. We denote by ūĚĒĹ\mathbb{F} and ūĚĒĺ\mathbb{G} the augmented filtration generated by (W,őĪ)(W,\alpha) and WW, respectively.

In this paper, we study the following infinite-horizon stochastic control problem:

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | J‚Äč(X)=ūĚĒľ‚Äč[‚ąę0‚ąěe‚ąíŌē‚Äčs‚Äč(‚ąíYs‚ąí‚Äčd‚ÄčXs+ő≥s2‚Äčd‚Äč[X]s‚ąíŌÉsőĪs‚Äčd‚Äč[X,W]s+őĽsőĪs‚ÄčXs2‚Äčd‚Äčs)]‚Üíminover¬†‚ÄčX,J(X)=\mathbb{E}\left[\int\_{0}^{\infty}e^{-\phi s}\left(-Y\_{s-}\,dX\_{s}+\frac{\gamma\_{s}}{2}\,d[X]\_{s}-\sigma\_{s}^{\alpha\_{s}}\,d[X,W]\_{s}+\lambda\_{s}^{\alpha\_{s}}X\_{s}^{2}\,ds\right)\right]\rightarrow\min\quad\textrm{over }X, |  | (1.1) |

subject to the state dynamics

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | {d‚ÄčYs=‚ąíŌĀsőĪs‚ÄčYs‚Äčd‚Äčs‚ąíő≥s‚Äčd‚ÄčXs+ŌÉsőĪs‚Äčd‚ÄčWs‚ąíd‚Äč[ő≥,X]s,X0‚ąí=x0,Y0‚ąí=y0,őĪ0‚ąí=i0,\left\{\begin{split}dY\_{s}&=-\rho\_{s}^{\alpha\_{s}}Y\_{s}\,ds-\gamma\_{s}\,dX\_{s}+\sigma\_{s}^{\alpha\_{s}}\,dW\_{s}-d[\gamma,X]\_{s},\\ X\_{0-}&=x\_{0},\quad\,Y\_{0-}=y\_{0},\quad\alpha\_{0-}=i\_{0},\end{split}\right. |  | (1.2) |

where ő≥\gamma follows the dynamics

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | d‚Äčő≥s=ő≥s‚Äč(őľs‚Äčd‚Äčs+ŌÉ1,s‚Äčd‚ÄčWs),ő≥0>0.d\gamma\_{s}=\gamma\_{s}\left(\mu\_{s}\,ds+\sigma\_{1,s}\,dW\_{s}\right),\quad\gamma\_{0}>0. |  | (1.3) |

The minimization in ([1.1](#S1.E1 "In 1 Introduction ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies")) is taken over all c√†dl√†g semimartingales subject to some integrability conditions that will be specified later.

The control problem ([1.1](#S1.E1 "In 1 Introduction ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies"))-([1.2](#S1.E2 "In 1 Introduction ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies")) without regime switching and with constant ő≥\gamma has been studied in [[8](#bib.bib8)], motivated by an optimal liquidation problem with semimartingale strategies and infinite horizon, where XX is the position of the player and YY is the price deviation process. Each term in the cost functional ([1.1](#S1.E1 "In 1 Introduction ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies")) is well interpreted by a micro-foundation; refer to [[8](#bib.bib8), Section 2.1] and [[20](#bib.bib20), Section 4.1] for details. While optimal trade execution typically focuses on short horizons, Almgren [[4](#bib.bib4)] and Sch√∂neborn [[26](#bib.bib26)] showed that removing temporal constraints fundamentally alters the optimal strategy, with certain model parameters even precluding full liquidation in finite time. Prompted by this funding, our recent work [[8](#bib.bib8)] investigates how strategies transform over extended horizons by analyzing the long-term behavior of a stochastic control problem with semimartingale strategies and external flows.
Similar models as ([1.1](#S1.E1 "In 1 Introduction ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies"))-([1.2](#S1.E2 "In 1 Introduction ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies")) without regime switching and with finite horizon are studied in Ackermann et al. [[1](#bib.bib1), [2](#bib.bib2), [3](#bib.bib3)] in different settings, with and without risk aversion, single asset or multiple asset.

The candidate value function and the optimal strategy can be characterized by three systems of infinite‚ÄĎhorizon BSDEs, one of which is a linear system with stochastic Lipschitz drivers that appears to be new to the literature. Our first contribution is to establish an existence result for a general class of infinite‚ÄĎhorizon BSDE systems with stochastic Lipschitz drivers, which is of independent interest.
To this end, we first truncate both the unbounded coefficients and the infinite time horizon. The resulting BSDE system has Lipschitz drivers on a finite horizon, and its well‚ÄĎposedness follows from standard results in the literature (see, e.g., [[6](#bib.bib6), Theorem 4.1]). However, the corresponding solutions lie only in standard solution spaces, and the associated a priori estimates depend explicitly on the time horizon. This dependence prevents a direct passage to the infinite‚ÄĎhorizon limit. To overcome this difficulty, we construct a time‚ÄĎweighted solution space by carefully choosing a discount factor so that the resulting a priori estimates are uniform with respect to the truncation index. To verify that solutions of the truncated system belong to this weighted space, we compare the system with a one‚ÄĎdimensional BSDE, rather than an ODE as is commonly done in the regime‚ÄĎswitching literature (see, e.g., [[11](#bib.bib11), [12](#bib.bib12)]). This comparison requires a delicate BMO analysis, including the use of energy inequalities and reverse H√∂lder inequalities. We then let the truncation index tend to infinity and verify that the limit solves the original infinite‚ÄĎhorizon system.

Our second contribution is the resolution of the stochastic control problem ([1.1](#S1.E1 "In 1 Introduction ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies"))‚Äď([1.2](#S1.E2 "In 1 Introduction ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies")). We first prove that the value function is finite, a fact that is not immediate from the original formulation of the cost functional ([1.1](#S1.E1 "In 1 Introduction ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies")). Our approach begins with the finite‚ÄĎhorizon counterpart, where the cost can be rewritten as the sum of a nonnegative quadratic term and the candidate value function. The infinite‚ÄĎhorizon cost is then shown to arise as the limit of this decomposition, with convergence relying crucially on the well‚ÄĎposedness results established in the first contribution. During the rewriting, to apply It√ī‚Äôs formula for processes with regime switching (see [[12](#bib.bib12), Lemma 4.3]), we must ensure that the relevant processes only jump as a result of regime‚ÄĎswitching. Motivated by [[1](#bib.bib1), [2](#bib.bib2)], we reexpress the cost functional in terms of the process P:=X+1ő≥‚ÄčYP:=X+\frac{1}{\gamma}Y, referred to as the scaled hidden deviation process. In our setting, all jumps of PP originate from the regime process őĪ\alpha. The existence of an optimal strategy is obtained under additional assumptions. The main challenge lies in proving admissibility of the candidate strategy. Again inspired by [[1](#bib.bib1), [2](#bib.bib2)], we estimate a process related to
PP rather than XX directly. Unlike [[1](#bib.bib1)], the corresponding SDE involves unbounded linear coefficients. We eliminate this difficulty via a suitable linear transformation, yielding an SDE with coefficients expressed through a stochastic exponential, for which effective estimates can be derived.

Our work can be compared with two strands of the literature.
First, [[15](#bib.bib15)] studies a linear‚Äďquadratic control problem with regime switching on a finite horizon. Their approach is based on a contraction mapping argument, which can be extended to the infinite‚ÄĎhorizon setting, albeit under the additional assumption that a certain discount factor must dominate a quantity related to the transition rates qi‚Äčjq^{ij}. In contrast, our approach to the analysis of general systems of linear BSDEs on an infinite horizon does not rely on such assumptions. Further discussion and technical details can be found in the first author‚Äôs PhD thesis[[7](#bib.bib7)]. Second, our work is related to the literature on multidimensional BSDEs with infinite horizons and unbounded coefficients; see, for example, [[17](#bib.bib17), [18](#bib.bib18), [19](#bib.bib19), [28](#bib.bib28)]. In particular, [[17](#bib.bib17)] establishes well‚ÄĎposedness for multidimensional BSDEs under a weak stochastic monotonicity condition, a general growth condition in yy, and a stochastic Lipschitz condition in
zz. The results in [[18](#bib.bib18)] refine this framework by integrating continuous dependence and comparison theorems within a unified proof. More recently, [[19](#bib.bib19)] develops existence results in weighted
L2L^{2}-spaces with random terminal times under similar stochastic monotonicity and Lipschitz conditions. A common feature of these works is the crucial assumption that
‚ąę0‚ąě(|ut|+vt2)‚ÄčūĚĎĎt<‚ąě\int\_{0}^{\infty}(|u\_{t}|+v\_{t}^{2})\,dt<\infty a.s.,
where uu and
vv denote the (possibly stochastic) coefficients of yy and
zz, respectively; see [[17](#bib.bib17), Section 2], [[18](#bib.bib18), Assumption (I3)], [[19](#bib.bib19), Inequality (1.10)], and [[28](#bib.bib28), Assumptions (A4)‚Äď(A5)]. In our setting, however, a key observation is that the coefficient of yy in the infinite‚ÄĎhorizon BSDE depends explicitly on the transition rates qi‚Äčjq^{ij}, causing this integrability condition to fail. In addition, an earlier work by Papapantoleon et al.¬†[[21](#bib.bib21)] studies a broader class of multidimensional BSDEs with unbounded random time horizons driven by general martingales, allowing for stochastic discontinuities in the filtration. Their model is formulated within a sophisticated and highly general framework, incorporating jumps and a general filtration. Nevertheless, when one abstracts from these structural features to focus on the core mechanism, their approach encounters a similar coefficient integrability issue to that identified in [[17](#bib.bib17), [18](#bib.bib18), [19](#bib.bib19), [28](#bib.bib28)] when applied to our setting. As a result, these existing frameworks cannot be directly applied without imposing additional restrictive assumptions. Filling this gap requires the development of new methodologies tailored to our systems of infinite‚ÄĎhorizon BSDEs with unbounded coefficients. We also note that techniques developed for multidimensional BSDEs with unbounded coefficients on finite horizons generally do not extend to our infinite‚ÄĎhorizon framework. For example, [[9](#bib.bib9)] studies multidimensional SDEs and BSDEs on finite horizons, driven by semimartingales and continuous local martingales, respectively, under suitable sliceability conditions in the BMO space for unbounded coefficients. However, these conditions are insufficient for our infinite‚ÄĎhorizon analysis. The underlying difficulty again stems from the constant transition rates
qi‚Äčjq^{ij}, which render the coefficient of
yy non‚ÄĎsliceable in the BMO space.

Before presenting the section‚ÄĎby‚ÄĎsection summary, we briefly review some existing results on optimal liquidation under regime switching; see [[5](#bib.bib5), [11](#bib.bib11), [22](#bib.bib22), [23](#bib.bib23), [27](#bib.bib27)]. Among these works, [[22](#bib.bib22)] employs regime switching to model stock price dynamics and studies an optimal liquidation problem formulated as an optimal stopping problem. In [[23](#bib.bib23)], the authors further allow the regime‚ÄĎswitching intensities to depend on the trading intensity and analyze an infinite‚ÄĎhorizon liquidation problem using viscosity solution techniques. The work [[5](#bib.bib5)] considers a finite‚ÄĎhorizon liquidation model incorporating both permanent and temporary price impact, again studied via a viscosity solution approach. In a discrete‚ÄĎtime setting, [[27](#bib.bib27)] investigates an optimal liquidation problem in which regime switching is used to model stochastic order book resilience. More recently, [[11](#bib.bib11)] analyzes a system of singular BSDEs arising from a liquidation problem, but restricts attention to the finite‚ÄĎhorizon case.
All of these studies differ from the focus of the present work, which centers on infinite‚ÄĎhorizon liquidation problems and their characterization through systems of BSDEs with unbounded coefficients.

The remainder of the paper is organized as follows. We conclude the introduction by introducing notation and stating the standing assumptions. Section [2](#S2 "2 Candidate BSDE systems ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies") formulates the candidate BSDE systems associated with the control problem ([1.1](#S1.E1 "In 1 Introduction ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies"))‚Äď([1.2](#S1.E2 "In 1 Introduction ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies")). Motivated by these systems, Section [3](#S3 "3 A general system of infinite horizon BSDEs with stochastic Lipschitz drivers ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies") is devoted to the analysis of a general class of infinite‚ÄĎhorizon BSDE systems with unbounded coefficients and establishes the corresponding well‚ÄĎposedness results. Finally, Section [4](#S4 "4 The solvability of the control problem (1.1)-(1.2) ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies") proves the solvability of the original control problem.

Convention.

1. 1.

   When the filtration, time horizon, and base space are clear from context, or when we do not want to emphasize the base space, we omit them from the space notation. For instance, we write L‚ąě,KL^{\infty,K} and HBMO2,KH^{2,K}\_{\mathrm{BMO}} as shorthand for L‚Ąć‚ąě,K‚Äč(0,‚ąě;ūĚíģ)L^{\infty,K}\_{\mathbb{H}}(0,\infty;\mathcal{S}) and HBMO,‚Ąć2,K‚Äč(0,‚ąě;ūĚíģ)H^{2,K}\_{\mathrm{BMO},\mathbb{H}}(0,\infty;\mathcal{S}), respectively, when ‚Ąć\mathbb{H}, [0,‚ąě)[0,\infty), and ūĚíģ\mathcal{S} are understood from context.
2. 2.

   The symbol cc denotes a positive constant that may vary from line to line, but is always independent of any sequence index tending to infinity.
3. 3.

   In subsequent estimates, we often omit vector indices by appealing to the Euclidean norm. For example, for a vector v:=(v1,‚Ä¶,v‚Ąď)v:=(v^{1},\dots,v^{\ell}), we frequently use the inequality

The following standing assumptions are assumed to hold throughout the paper.

###### Assumption 1.1.

The discount factor Ōē\phi is a nonnegative constant. For each i‚ąą‚Ą≥i\in\cal M, assume that ŌÉi\sigma^{i}, ŌĀi\rho^{i}, őĽi\lambda^{i}, őľ\mu and ŌÉ1\sigma\_{1} belong to ūĚíęūĚĒĺ‚Äč(‚ĄĚ)\mathcal{P}\_{\mathbb{G}}(\mathbb{R}). Moreover,
there exist positive constants ő≤\beta, c^\hat{c}, LL and ŌĶ\epsilon such that for any t‚ąą[0,‚ąě)t\in[0,\infty) and i‚ąą‚Ą≥i\in\cal M, it holds

1. (i)

   |ŌĀti|‚Č§c^|\rho^{i}\_{t}|\leq\hat{c} and 0‚Č§őĽtiő≥t‚Č§c^0\leq\frac{\lambda^{i}\_{t}}{\gamma\_{t}}\leq\hat{c},
2. (ii)

   |őľt|‚Č§c^‚Äče‚ąíL‚Äčt|\mu\_{t}|\leq\hat{c}e^{-Lt} and |ŌÉ1,t|‚Č§c^‚Äče‚ąíL‚Äčt|\sigma\_{1,t}|\leq\hat{c}e^{-Lt} and |ŌÉ~ti|‚Č§c^‚Äče‚ąíő≤‚Äčt2|\widetilde{\sigma}^{i}\_{t}|\leq\hat{c}e^{-\frac{\beta t}{2}} where ŌÉ~ti:=e‚ąíŌē‚Äčt2‚ÄčŌÉti\widetilde{\sigma}^{i}\_{t}:=e^{-\frac{\phi t}{2}}\sigma^{i}\_{t},
3. (iii)

   Ōē2+ŌĀti+őľt2‚ąíŌÉ1,t22‚Č•ŌĶ\frac{\phi}{2}+\rho^{i}\_{t}+\frac{\mu\_{t}}{2}-\frac{\sigma\_{1,t}^{2}}{2}\geq\epsilon, ŌĀti+őľt‚ąíŌÉ1,t2‚Č•0\rho^{i}\_{t}+\mu\_{t}-\sigma\_{1,t}^{2}\geq 0 and Ōē2+őĽtiő≥t‚Äč(ŌĀti+őľt)őľt2+ŌĀti+őĽtiő≥t+Ōē2‚Č•ŌĶ\frac{\phi}{2}+\frac{\frac{\lambda\_{t}^{i}}{\gamma\_{t}}(\rho\_{t}^{i}+\mu\_{t})}{\frac{\mu\_{t}}{2}+\rho\_{t}^{i}+\frac{\lambda\_{t}^{i}}{\gamma\_{t}}+\frac{\phi}{2}}\geq\epsilon.

The space of admissible strategies.
The admissible space for ([1.1](#S1.E1 "In 1 Introduction ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies"))-([1.2](#S1.E2 "In 1 Introduction ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies")), denoted by ūĚíú\mathscr{A}, is defined as all X‚ąąūĚíęūĚĒĹ‚Äč(‚ĄĚ)X\in\mathcal{P}\_{\mathbb{F}}(\mathbb{R}) satisfying

1. (i)

   XX is a c√†dl√†g semimartingale;
2. (ii)

   the following integrability is satisfied by X~\widetilde{X}

   |  |  |  |  |
   | --- | --- | --- | --- |
   |  | ūĚĒľ‚Äč[supt‚Č•0e2‚ÄčŌÜ‚Äčt‚Äčő≥t‚ÄčX~t2]<‚ąě,\mathbb{E}\left[\sup\_{t\geq 0}e^{2\varphi t}\gamma\_{t}\widetilde{X}\_{t}^{2}\right]<\infty, |  | (1.4) |

   respectively,

   |  |  |  |  |
   | --- | --- | --- | --- |
   |  | ūĚĒľ‚Äč[supt‚Č•0e4‚ÄčŌÜ‚Äčt‚Äčő≥t2‚ÄčP~t4]<‚ąě,\mathbb{E}\left[\sup\_{t\geq 0}e^{4\varphi t}\gamma\_{t}^{2}\widetilde{P}\_{t}^{4}\right]<\infty, |  | (1.5) |

where 0<ŌÜ<ŌĶ‚ąßő≤80<\varphi<\epsilon\wedge\frac{\beta}{8}, X~s:=e‚ąíŌē2‚Äčs‚ÄčXs\widetilde{X}\_{s}:=e^{-\frac{\phi}{2}s}X\_{s}, Y~s:=e‚ąíŌē2‚Äčs‚ÄčYs\widetilde{Y}\_{s}:=e^{-\frac{\phi}{2}s}Y\_{s} and P~s:=X~s+1ő≥s‚ÄčY~s\widetilde{P}\_{s}:=\widetilde{X}\_{s}+\frac{1}{\gamma\_{s}}\widetilde{Y}\_{s}.

Due to the one-to-one correspondence between XX and X~\widetilde{X}, we may abuse the notation by writing X~‚ąąūĚíú\widetilde{X}\in\mathcal{A} for simplicity, if XX satisfies (i) and X~\widetilde{X} satisfies (ii).

## 2 Candidate BSDE systems

In this section, we formulate the system of backward stochastic differential equations (BSDEs) associated with the control problem under study. We begin by reformulating the optimal control problem ([1.1](#S1.E1 "In 1 Introduction ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies"))‚Äď([1.2](#S1.E2 "In 1 Introduction ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies")) in dynamic matrix form:

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | J‚Äč(t,ūĚí≥t‚ąí,i;X~)=ūĚĒľt‚Äč[‚ąęt‚ąě(ūĚí≥s‚ä§‚Äč‚Ąí‚Äčd‚ÄčX~s+‚Ąõs‚Äčd‚Äč[X~]s+‚Ąí‚ä§‚ÄčūĚíüsőĪs‚Äčd‚Äč[X~,W]s+ūĚí≥s‚ä§‚ÄčūĚí¨sőĪs‚ÄčūĚí≥s‚Äčd‚Äčs)],J(t,\mathcal{X}\_{t-},i;\widetilde{X})=\mathbb{E}\_{t}\left[\int\_{t}^{\infty}\left(\mathcal{X}\_{s}^{\top}\mathcal{L}d\widetilde{X}\_{s}+\mathcal{R}\_{s}\,d[\widetilde{X}]\_{s}+\mathcal{L}^{\top}\mathcal{D}\_{s}^{\alpha\_{s}}\,d[\widetilde{X},W]\_{s}+\mathcal{X}\_{s}^{\top}\mathcal{Q}\_{s}^{\alpha\_{s}}\mathcal{X}\_{s}\,ds\right)\right], |  | (2.1) |

subject to the controlled state dynamics

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | d‚ÄčūĚí≥s=‚ĄčsőĪs‚ÄčūĚí≥s‚Äčd‚Äčs+ūĚíüsőĪs‚Äčd‚ÄčWs+‚Ąźs‚Äčd‚ÄčX~s+ūĚíęs‚Äčd‚Äč[X~,W]s,s‚ąą[t,‚ąě),d\mathcal{X}\_{s}=\mathcal{H}\_{s}^{\alpha\_{s}}\mathcal{X}\_{s}ds+\mathcal{D}\_{s}^{\alpha\_{s}}dW\_{s}+\mathcal{I}\_{s}d\widetilde{X}\_{s}+\mathcal{P}\_{s}d[\widetilde{X},W]\_{s},\quad s\in[t,\infty), |  | (2.2) |

where ūĚí≥=(X~,Y~)‚ä§\mathcal{X}=(\widetilde{X},\widetilde{Y})^{\top}.
The coefficient matrices are defined as follows:

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | ‚Ąí=(0‚ąí1)‚ä§,‚Ąõs=ő≥s2,ūĚíüsőĪs=(0ŌÉ~sőĪs)‚ä§,‚Ąźs=(1‚ąíő≥s)‚ä§,ūĚí¨sőĪs=(őĽsőĪs‚ąíŌē4‚ąíŌē40),‚ĄčsőĪs=(00‚ąíŌē2‚Äčő≥s‚ąíŌĀsőĪs‚ąíŌē2),ūĚíęs=(0‚ąíő≥s‚ÄčŌÉ1,s)‚ä§.\begin{split}\mathcal{L}=&~\begin{pmatrix}0&-1\end{pmatrix}^{\top},\qquad\mathcal{R}\_{s}=\frac{\gamma\_{s}}{2},\qquad\mathcal{D}\_{s}^{\alpha\_{s}}=\begin{pmatrix}0&\widetilde{\sigma}\_{s}^{\alpha\_{s}}\end{pmatrix}^{\top},\qquad\mathcal{I}\_{s}=\begin{pmatrix}1&-\gamma\_{s}\end{pmatrix}^{\top},\\ \mathcal{Q}\_{s}^{\alpha\_{s}}=&~\begin{pmatrix}\lambda\_{s}^{\alpha\_{s}}&-\frac{\phi}{4}\\ -\frac{\phi}{4}&0\end{pmatrix},\qquad\mathcal{H}\_{s}^{\alpha\_{s}}=\begin{pmatrix}0&0\\ -\frac{\phi}{2}\gamma\_{s}&-\rho\_{s}^{\alpha\_{s}}-\frac{\phi}{2}\end{pmatrix},\qquad\mathcal{P}\_{s}=\begin{pmatrix}0&-\gamma\_{s}\sigma\_{1,s}\end{pmatrix}^{\top}.\end{split} |  | (2.3) |

Using either a discrete-time approximation approach (see [[1](#bib.bib1), [10](#bib.bib10)]) or a transformation to a linear-quadratic control framework (see [[2](#bib.bib2)]), we now present three systems of infinite-horizon BSDEs that will play a fundamental role in establishing well-posedness and in characterizing both the value function and the optimal strategy.

‚ąô\bullet Let A:=(Ai)i=1,‚Ä¶,‚ĄďA:=(A^{i})\_{i=1,\dots,\ell} be a vector of symmetric ‚ĄĚ2√ó2\mathbb{R}^{2\times 2}-valued processes satisfying A11i=ő≥‚ÄčA21iA^{i}\_{11}=\gamma A^{i}\_{21} and A12i=ő≥‚ÄčA22i+12A^{i}\_{12}=\gamma A^{i}\_{22}+\frac{1}{2} for each i‚ąą‚Ą≥i\in\mathcal{M}. Define A¬Įi:=A12i\bar{A}^{i}:=A^{i}\_{12}, and suppose (A¬Įi)i‚ąą‚Ą≥(\bar{A}^{i})\_{i\in\mathcal{M}} satisfies the following system of BSDEs on [0,‚ąě)[0,\infty):

|  |  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | ‚ąíd‚ÄčA¬Įsi=\displaystyle-d\bar{A}^{i}\_{s}= | {‚ąĎj=1‚Ąďqi‚Äčj‚ÄčA¬Įsj+(őľs‚ąíŌē)‚ÄčA¬Įsi+ŌÉ1,s‚ÄčZsA¬Į,i+őĽsiő≥s‚ąíő≥sasi‚Äč((őľs+ŌĀsi)‚ÄčA¬Įsi+ŌÉ1,s‚ÄčZsA¬Į,i+őĽsiő≥s)2}‚Äčd‚Äčs\displaystyle~\left\{\sum^{\ell}\_{j=1}q^{ij}\bar{A}\_{s}^{j}+(\mu\_{s}-\phi)\bar{A}^{i}\_{s}+\sigma\_{1,s}Z^{\bar{A},i}\_{s}+\frac{\lambda\_{s}^{i}}{\gamma\_{s}}-\frac{\gamma\_{s}}{a^{i}\_{s}}\left((\mu\_{s}+\rho\_{s}^{i})\bar{A}\_{s}^{i}+\sigma\_{1,s}Z^{\bar{A},i}\_{s}+\frac{\lambda\_{s}^{i}}{\gamma\_{s}}\right)^{2}\right\}\,ds |  | (2.4) |
|  |  | ‚ąíZsA¬Į,i‚Äčd‚ÄčWs,\displaystyle~-Z^{\bar{A},i}\_{s}\,dW\_{s}, |  |

with the transversality condition

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | limT‚Üí‚ąěūĚĒľ‚Äč[e‚ąíp‚ÄčKA¬Į‚ÄčT‚Äč|A¬ĮTi|p]=0¬†for any¬†‚ÄčKA¬Į>0,p‚Č•1,i‚ąą‚Ą≥.\lim\limits\_{T\to\infty}\mathbb{E}\left[e^{-pK\_{\bar{A}}T}|\bar{A}^{i}\_{T}|^{p}\right]=0\quad\text{ for any }K\_{\bar{A}}>0,\,p\geq 1,\,i\in\cal M. |  | (2.5) |

Here, the auxiliary coefficient aa that will be used frequently throughout the paper is defined as

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | ati=ő≥t‚ÄčŌÉ1,t2‚ÄčA¬Įti+őľt‚Äčő≥t2‚ąíő≥t‚ÄčŌÉ1,t22+ő≥t‚ÄčŌĀti+őĽti+Ōē‚Äčő≥t2.a\_{t}^{i}=\gamma\_{t}\sigma\_{1,t}^{2}\bar{A}\_{t}^{i}+\frac{\mu\_{t}\gamma\_{t}}{2}-\frac{\gamma\_{t}\sigma\_{1,t}^{2}}{2}+\gamma\_{t}\rho\_{t}^{i}+\lambda\_{t}^{i}+\frac{\phi\gamma\_{t}}{2}. |  | (2.6) |

‚ąô\bullet Let B:=(Bi)i‚ąą‚Ą≥=((B1i,B2i)‚ä§)i‚ąą‚Ą≥B:=(B^{i})\_{i\in\mathcal{M}}=((B^{i}\_{1},B^{i}\_{2})^{\top})\_{i\in\mathcal{M}} be a vector of ‚ĄĚ2√ó1\mathbb{R}^{2\times 1}-valued processes satisfying B1i=ő≥‚ÄčB2iB^{i}\_{1}=\gamma B^{i}\_{2}. Define B¬Įi:=B1i\bar{B}^{i}:=B^{i}\_{1}, and suppose (B¬Įi)i‚ąą‚Ą≥(\bar{B}^{i})\_{i\in\mathcal{M}} satisfies the following system of BSDEs on [0,‚ąě)[0,\infty):

|  |  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | ‚ąíd‚ÄčB¬Įsi=\displaystyle-d\bar{B}^{i}\_{s}= | {‚ąĎj=1‚Ąďqi‚ÄčjB¬Įsj‚ąíŌē2B¬Įsi+2ŌÉ~siZsA¬Į,i‚ąíő≥sasi((őľs+ŌĀsi)A¬Įsi+ŌÉ1,sZsA¬Į,i+őĽsiő≥s)\displaystyle~\left\{\sum^{\ell}\_{j=1}q^{ij}\bar{B}\_{s}^{j}-\frac{\phi}{2}\bar{B}^{i}\_{s}+2\widetilde{\sigma}^{i}\_{s}Z^{\bar{A},i}\_{s}-\frac{\gamma\_{s}}{a^{i}\_{s}}\left((\mu\_{s}+\rho\_{s}^{i})\bar{A}\_{s}^{i}+\sigma\_{1,s}Z^{\bar{A},i}\_{s}+\frac{\lambda\_{s}^{i}}{\gamma\_{s}}\right)\right. |  | (2.7) |
|  |  | √ó((ŌĀsi+őľs‚ąíŌÉ1,s2)B¬Įsi+2ŌÉ1,sŌÉ~siA¬Įsi‚ąíŌÉ1,sŌÉ~si+ŌÉ1,sZsB¬Į,i)}ds‚ąíZB¬Į,isdWs,\displaystyle~\quad\times\left((\rho\_{s}^{i}+\mu\_{s}-\sigma\_{1,s}^{2})\bar{B}^{i}\_{s}+2\sigma\_{1,s}\widetilde{\sigma}\_{s}^{i}\bar{A}\_{s}^{i}-\sigma\_{1,s}\widetilde{\sigma}\_{s}^{i}+\sigma\_{1,s}Z^{\bar{B},i}\_{s}\right)\Bigg\}\,ds-Z^{\bar{B},i}\_{s}\,dW\_{s}, |  |

## 3 A general system of infinite horizon BSDEs with stochastic Lipschitz drivers

Motivated by the systems of BSDEs introduced in Section¬†[2](#S2 "2 Candidate BSDE systems ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies"), particularly the infinite-horizon systems ([2.7](#S2.E7 "In 2 Candidate BSDE systems ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies"))-([2.10](#S2.E10 "In 2 Candidate BSDE systems ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies")), we study a general class of infinite-horizon BSDEs with stochastic Lipschitz drivers. The systems ([2.7](#S2.E7 "In 2 Candidate BSDE systems ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies")), ([2.9](#S2.E9 "In 2 Candidate BSDE systems ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies")) will appear as a special case of this general framework. The results presented in this section are of independent interest. Before stating the main theorem, we first state several preliminary lemmas.

### 3.1 Preliminary lemmas

###### Lemma 3.1.

Assume ő∂‚ąąHBMO2,Kő∂\zeta\in H^{2,K\_{\zeta}}\_{\text{BMO}}, where Kő∂K\_{\zeta} is a given constant.
For any b1‚ąą(0,2)b\_{1}\in(0,2), b2>0b\_{2}>0 and b3>Kő∂b\_{3}>K\_{\zeta}, it holds that

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | ‚ÄĖe‚ąíb1‚Äčb3‚Ā£‚čÖ‚Äč|ő∂‚čÖ|b1‚ÄĖb2,e‚Äčx‚Äčp:=ess‚ÄčsupŌČ‚ąąő©,ŌĄ‚ąąūĚíĮ‚Ā°ūĚĒľŌĄ‚Äč[exp‚Ā°(b2‚Äč‚ąęŌĄ‚ąěe‚ąíb1‚Äčb3‚Äčs‚Äč|ő∂s|b1‚ÄčūĚĎĎs)]‚Č§43‚Äčexp‚Ā°{(12‚Äčb1‚ÄčN2)‚ąíb1‚Äčq2‚Äčb2qb1‚Äčq2‚Äč(b3‚ąíKő∂)},\begin{split}\left\|e^{-b\_{1}b\_{3}\cdot}|\zeta\_{\cdot}|^{b\_{1}}\right\|\_{b\_{2},exp}:=&~\operatorname\*{ess\,sup}\_{\omega\in\Omega,\tau\in\cal T}\mathbb{E}\_{\tau}\left[\exp\left(b\_{2}\int^{\infty}\_{\tau}e^{-b\_{1}b\_{3}s}|\zeta\_{s}|^{b\_{1}}\,ds\right)\right]\\ \leq&~\frac{4}{3}\exp\left\{\left(\frac{1}{2b\_{1}N^{2}}\right)^{-\frac{b\_{1}q}{2}}\frac{b\_{2}^{q}}{b\_{1}q^{2}(b\_{3}-K\_{\zeta})}\right\},\end{split} |  | (3.1) |

where qq is the conjugate of 2b1\frac{2}{b\_{1}}, and NN is any positive constant such that

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | ‚ÄĖő∂‚ÄĖBMO,Kő∂‚Č§N.\left\|\zeta\right\|\_{\text{BMO},K\_{\zeta}}\leq N. |  | (3.2) |

###### Proof.

Given ő∂‚ąąHBMO2,Kő∂\zeta\in H^{2,K\_{\zeta}}\_{\text{BMO}} and ([3.2](#S3.E2 "In Lemma 3.1. ‚Ä£ 3.1 Preliminary lemmas ‚Ä£ 3 A general system of infinite horizon BSDEs with stochastic Lipschitz drivers ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies")),
by [[16](#bib.bib16), Theorem 2.2] we have for each ŌĄ‚ąąūĚíĮ\tau\in\mathcal{T}

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  | ūĚĒľŌĄ‚Äč[exp‚Ā°(14‚ÄčN2‚Äč‚ąęŌĄ‚ąěe‚ąí2‚ÄčKő∂‚Äčs‚Äč|ő∂s|2‚ÄčūĚĎĎs)]‚Č§11‚ąí‚ÄĖ‚ąę0‚čÖ12‚ÄčN‚Äče‚ąíKő∂‚Äčs‚Äčő∂s‚ÄčūĚĎĎWs‚ÄĖBMO2‚Č§11‚ąí14=43.\mathbb{E}\_{\tau}\left[\exp\left(\frac{1}{4N^{2}}\int^{\infty}\_{\tau}e^{-2K\_{\zeta}s}|\zeta\_{s}|^{2}\,ds\right)\right]\leq\frac{1}{1-\|\int^{\cdot}\_{0}\frac{1}{2N}e^{-K\_{\zeta}s}\zeta\_{s}\,dW\_{s}\|^{2}\_{\text{BMO}}}\leq\frac{1}{1-\frac{1}{4}}=\frac{4}{3}. |  |

Thus, by Young‚Äôs inequality we have

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  |  | supŌĄūĚĒľŌĄ‚Äč[exp‚Ā°{b2‚Äč‚ąęŌĄ‚ąěe‚ąíb1‚Äčb3‚Äčs‚Äč|ő∂s|b1‚ÄčūĚĎĎs}]\displaystyle~\sup\_{\tau}\mathbb{E}\_{\tau}\left[\exp\left\{b\_{2}\int^{\infty}\_{\tau}e^{-b\_{1}b\_{3}s}|\zeta\_{s}|^{b\_{1}}\,ds\right\}\right] |  |
|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | =\displaystyle= | supŌĄūĚĒľŌĄ‚Äč[exp‚Ā°{‚ąęŌĄ‚ąě((2b1‚čÖ14‚ÄčN2)b12‚Äče‚ąíb1‚ÄčKő∂‚Äčs‚Äč|ő∂s|b1√ó(2b1‚čÖ14‚ÄčN2)‚ąíb12‚Äčb2‚Äče‚ąíb1‚Äč(b3‚ąíKő∂)‚Äčs)‚ÄčūĚĎĎs}]\displaystyle~\sup\_{\tau}\mathbb{E}\_{\tau}\left[\exp\left\{\int^{\infty}\_{\tau}\left(\left(\frac{2}{b\_{1}}\cdot\frac{1}{4N^{2}}\right)^{\frac{b\_{1}}{2}}e^{-b\_{1}K\_{\zeta}s}|\zeta\_{s}|^{b\_{1}}\times\left(\frac{2}{b\_{1}}\cdot\frac{1}{4N^{2}}\right)^{-\frac{b\_{1}}{2}}b\_{2}e^{-b\_{1}(b\_{3}-K\_{\zeta})s}\right)\,ds\right\}\right] |  |
|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | ‚Č§\displaystyle\leq | supŌĄūĚĒľŌĄ‚Äč[exp‚Ā°{‚ąęŌĄ‚ąě(14‚ÄčN2‚Äče‚ąí2‚ÄčKő∂‚Äčs‚Äč|ő∂s|2+1q‚Äč(2b1‚čÖ14‚ÄčN2)‚ąíb1‚Äčq2‚Äčb2q‚Äče‚ąíb1‚Äčq‚Äč(b3‚ąíKő∂)‚Äčs)‚ÄčūĚĎĎs}](where¬†‚Äč1q+12/b1=1)\displaystyle~\sup\_{\tau}\mathbb{E}\_{\tau}\left[\exp\left\{\int^{\infty}\_{\tau}\left(\frac{1}{4N^{2}}e^{-2K\_{\zeta}s}|\zeta\_{s}|^{2}+\frac{1}{q}\left(\frac{2}{b\_{1}}\cdot\frac{1}{4N^{2}}\right)^{-\frac{b\_{1}q}{2}}b\_{2}^{q}e^{-b\_{1}q(b\_{3}-K\_{\zeta})s}\right)\,ds\right\}\right]\quad\left(\text{where }\frac{1}{q}+\frac{1}{2/b\_{1}}=1\right) |  |
|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | ‚Č§\displaystyle\leq | 43‚Äčexp‚Ā°{(12‚Äčb1‚ÄčN2)‚ąíb1‚Äčq2‚Äčb2qb1‚Äčq2‚Äč(b3‚ąíKő∂)}.\displaystyle~\frac{4}{3}\exp\left\{\left(\frac{1}{2b\_{1}N^{2}}\right)^{-\frac{b\_{1}q}{2}}\frac{b\_{2}^{q}}{b\_{1}q^{2}(b\_{3}-K\_{\zeta})}\right\}. |  |

‚ąé

The following lemma can be found in [[16](#bib.bib16), Page 29].

###### Lemma 3.2 (Energy inequality).

Assume Z‚ąąHBMO2,0Z\in H^{2,0}\_{\text{BMO}}. For any constant n‚ąą‚Ąē+n\in\mathbb{N}\_{+}, it holds that

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | ess‚ÄčsupŌČ,ŌĄ‚Ā°ūĚĒľŌĄ‚Äč[(‚ąęŌĄ‚ąě|Zs|2‚ÄčūĚĎĎs)n]‚Č§n!‚Äč‚ÄĖZ‚ÄĖBMO2‚Äčn.\operatorname\*{ess\,sup}\_{\omega,\tau}\mathbb{E}\_{\tau}\left[\left(\int^{\infty}\_{\tau}|Z\_{s}|^{2}\,ds\right)^{n}\right]\leq n!\left\|Z\right\|^{2n}\_{\text{BMO}}. |  | (3.3) |

The following reverse H√∂lder inequality can be found in [[16](#bib.bib16), Theorem 3.1].

###### Lemma 3.3 (Reverse H√∂lder inequality).

Let ő¶\Phi be the function on (1,‚ąě)(1,\infty) defined as

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  | ő¶‚Äč(x)=(1+1x2‚Äčlog‚Ā°2‚Äčx‚ąí12‚Äč(x‚ąí1))1/2‚ąí1,\Phi(x)=\left(1+\frac{1}{x^{2}}\log\frac{2x-1}{2(x-1)}\right)^{1/2}-1, |  |

which is nonincreasing, limx‚Üė1ő¶‚Äč(x)=‚ąě\lim\_{x\searrow 1}\Phi(x)=\infty and limx‚Üó‚ąěő¶‚Äč(x)=0\lim\_{x\nearrow\infty}\Phi(x)=0.
Let Z‚ąąHBMO2,0Z\in H^{2,0}\_{\text{BMO}} and q‚ąó=ő¶‚ąí1‚Äč(‚ÄĖZ‚ÄĖBMO)q\_{\*}=\Phi^{-1}(\|Z\|\_{\text{BMO}}). For any 1<q<q‚ąó1<q<q\_{\*}, it holds that

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  | ess‚ÄčsupŌĄ‚ąąūĚíĮ‚Ā°ūĚĒľŌĄ‚Äč[|‚Ąį‚Äč(Z)‚ąě‚Ąį‚Äč(Z)ŌĄ|q]‚Č§ūĚí¶‚Äč(q,‚ÄĖZ‚ÄĖBMO),\operatorname\*{ess\,sup}\_{\tau\in\cal T}\mathbb{E}\_{\tau}\left[\left|\frac{\mathcal{E}(Z)\_{\infty}}{\mathcal{E}(Z)\_{\tau}}\right|^{q}\right]\leq\mathcal{K}(q,\|Z\|\_{\text{BMO}}), |  |

where

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  | ūĚí¶‚Äč(q,O)=21‚ąí2‚Äč(q‚ąí1)2‚Äčq‚ąí1‚Äčexp‚Ā°{q2‚Äč(O2+2‚ÄčO)}.\mathcal{K}(q,O)=\frac{2}{1-\frac{2(q-1)}{2q-1}\exp\left\{q^{2}(O^{2}+2O)\right\}}. |  |

### 3.2 A general infinite-horizon BSDE system

The goal of this section is to establish the existence of solutions to the following infinite-horizon BSDE system:

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | {‚ąíd‚ÄčYti=[‚ąíőĹti‚ÄčYti+‚ąĎj=1‚Ąďqi‚Äčj‚ÄčYtj+‚ąĎj=1‚Ąďőļti‚Äčj‚ÄčYtj+(gti)‚ä§‚ÄčZti+fti]‚Äčd‚Äčt‚ąí(Zti)‚ä§‚Äčd‚ÄčūĚí≤t,i‚ąą‚Ą≥,\left\{\begin{aligned} -dY^{i}\_{t}=&\left[-\nu^{i}\_{t}Y^{i}\_{t}+\sum^{\ell}\_{j=1}q^{ij}Y^{j}\_{t}+\sum^{\ell}\_{j=1}\kappa^{ij}\_{t}Y^{j}\_{t}+(g^{i}\_{t})^{\top}Z^{i}\_{t}+f^{i}\_{t}\right]\,dt-(Z^{i}\_{t})^{\top}\,d\mathcal{W}\_{t},\\ i\in&~\cal M,\end{aligned}\right. |  | (3.4) |

where ūĚí≤\mathcal{W} is a multidimensional Brownian motion.

The following assumptions on the coefficients of ([3.4](#S3.E4 "In 3.2 A general infinite-horizon BSDE system ‚Ä£ 3 A general system of infinite horizon BSDEs with stochastic Lipschitz drivers ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies")) are assumed to hold throughout Section [3.2](#S3.SS2 "3.2 A general infinite-horizon BSDE system ‚Ä£ 3 A general system of infinite horizon BSDEs with stochastic Lipschitz drivers ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies").

###### Assumption 3.4.

1. (i)

   Let r‚ąą(0,2)r\in(0,2), K¬Į‚Č§c¬Į\bar{K}\leq\bar{c} be fixed constants throughout this section555Notice that K¬Į\bar{K} and c¬Į\bar{c} can be either positive or negative.. All coefficients are assumed to be ‚ĄĪ√ó[0,‚ąě)\mathscr{F}\times[0,\infty) progressively measurable, where ‚ĄĪ\mathscr{F} denotes the augmented natural filtration of the Brownian motion ūĚí≤\mathcal{W}.
2. (ii)

   g‚ąąHBMO2,0g\in H^{2,0}\_{\text{BMO}}.
3. (iii)

   Let őļ:=(őļi‚Äčj)i,j‚ąą‚Ą≥‚ąąūĚíę‚ĄĪ‚Äč(‚ĄĚ‚Ąď√ó‚Ąď)\kappa:=(\kappa^{ij})\_{i,j\in\cal M}\in\mathcal{P}\_{\mathscr{F}}(\mathbb{R}^{\ell\times\ell}) satisfy őļi‚Äčj‚Č•0‚Äč¬†for¬†‚Äči‚Č†j‚Äč¬†and¬†‚Äč|őļ|‚Č§|Ōē|r\kappa^{ij}\geq 0\text{ for }i\neq j\text{ and }|\kappa|\leq|\phi|^{r}666This condition is required for the monotonicity in comparison principle for multidimensional BSDEs.  where Ōē‚ąąHBMO2,KŌē\phi\in H^{2,K\_{\phi}}\_{\text{BMO}} for KŌē<0K\_{\phi}<0.
4. (iv)

   Let őĹ:=(őĹi)i‚ąą‚Ą≥‚ąąūĚíę‚ĄĪ‚Äč(‚ĄĚ‚Ąď)\nu:=(\nu^{i})\_{i\in\cal M}\in\mathcal{P}\_{\mathscr{F}}(\mathbb{R}^{\ell}) satisfy K¬Į‚Č§őĹi‚Č§c¬Į‚Äč¬†for each¬†‚Äči‚ąą‚Ą≥.\bar{K}\leq\nu^{i}\leq\bar{c}\text{ for each }i\in\cal M.
5. (v)

   Given a constant Kf<K¬ĮK\_{f}<\bar{K}, |f|1/2‚ąą‚čāp‚Č•1Mp,Kf/2|f|^{1/2}\in\bigcap\_{p\geq 1}M^{p,K\_{f}/2}.

We will first establish the existence of solutions to a truncated version of ([3.4](#S3.E4 "In 3.2 A general infinite-horizon BSDE system ‚Ä£ 3 A general system of infinite horizon BSDEs with stochastic Lipschitz drivers ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies")), and second, show that this solution converges to one solution to ([3.4](#S3.E4 "In 3.2 A general infinite-horizon BSDE system ‚Ä£ 3 A general system of infinite horizon BSDEs with stochastic Lipschitz drivers ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies")) with some transversality condition.

For each given constant m>0m>0, define777We abuse the notation by letting hmh\_{m} denote functions on both ‚ĄĚ\mathbb{R} and ‚ĄĚ‚Ąď\mathbb{R}^{\ell}, without confusion.

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  | hm‚Äč(x):=min‚Ā°{|x|,m}|x|‚čÖx‚čÖūĚüŹ{|x|‚Č†0}h\_{m}(x):=\frac{\min\{|x|,m\}}{|x|}\cdot x\cdot\mathbf{1}\_{\{|x|\neq 0\}} |  |

and consider the truncated version of ([3.4](#S3.E4 "In 3.2 A general infinite-horizon BSDE system ‚Ä£ 3 A general system of infinite horizon BSDEs with stochastic Lipschitz drivers ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies"))

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | {‚ąíd‚ÄčYtm,i=[‚ąíőĹti‚ÄčYtm,i+‚ąĎj=1‚Ąďqi‚Äčj‚ÄčYtm,j+‚ąĎj=1‚Ąďhm‚Äč(őļti‚Äčj)‚ÄčYtm,j+hm‚Äč(gti)‚ä§‚ÄčZtm,i+fti]‚Äčd‚Äčt‚ąí(Ztm,i)‚ä§‚Äčd‚ÄčūĚí≤t,t‚ąą[0,m),Ytm,i=0,t‚ąą[m,‚ąě),i‚ąą‚Ą≥.\left\{\begin{aligned} -dY^{m,i}\_{t}=&~\left[-\nu^{i}\_{t}Y^{m,i}\_{t}+\sum^{\ell}\_{j=1}q^{ij}Y^{m,j}\_{t}+\sum^{\ell}\_{j=1}h\_{m}(\kappa^{ij}\_{t})Y^{m,j}\_{t}+h\_{m}(g^{i}\_{t})^{\top}Z^{m,i}\_{t}+f^{i}\_{t}\right]\,dt\\ &~-(Z^{m,i}\_{t})^{\top}\,d\mathcal{W}\_{t},\quad t\in[0,m),\\ Y^{m,i}\_{t}=&~0,\quad t\in[m,\infty),\\ i\in&~\cal M.\end{aligned}\right. |  | (3.5) |

The following lemma establishes both the existence of a solution to ([3.5](#S3.E5 "In 3.2 A general infinite-horizon BSDE system ‚Ä£ 3 A general system of infinite horizon BSDEs with stochastic Lipschitz drivers ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies")) and an a priori estimate for that solution, uniformly in mm.

###### Lemma 3.5.

For each mm, each K‚ąą(Kf,K¬Į)K\in(K\_{f},\bar{K}) and each K‚Ä≤>KK^{\prime}>K, the system of infinite-horizon BSDEs ([3.5](#S3.E5 "In 3.2 A general infinite-horizon BSDE system ‚Ä£ 3 A general system of infinite horizon BSDEs with stochastic Lipschitz drivers ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies")) admits a solution

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  | (Ym,Zm):=(Ym,i,Zm,i)i‚ąą‚Ą≥‚ąą‚čāp‚Č•1Sp,K√óM2,K‚Ä≤.(Y^{m},Z^{m}):=(Y^{m,i},Z^{m,i})\_{i\in\mathcal{M}}\in\bigcap\_{p\geq 1}S^{p,K}\times M^{2,K^{\prime}}. |  |

Moreover, for YmY^{m} we have the following estimate for any p>2‚Äčap>2a

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | ūĚĒľ‚Äč[supt‚Č•0|e‚ąíK‚Äčt‚ÄčYtm|p]‚Č§c‚ÄčūĚí¶‚Äč(q,N¬Į)pq‚Äč‚ÄĖ|Ōē|r‚ÄĖ2‚Äča‚Äč‚Ąď,e‚Äčx‚Äčpp2‚Äča‚ÄčūĚĒľ‚Äč[(‚ąę0‚ąěe‚ąíKf‚Äčs‚Äč|fs|‚ÄčūĚĎĎs)p],\begin{split}\mathbb{E}\left[\sup\_{t\geq 0}\left|e^{-Kt}Y^{m}\_{t}\right|^{p}\right]\leq c\mathcal{K}(q,\bar{N})^{\frac{p}{q}}\left\||\phi|^{r}\right\|^{\frac{p}{2a}}\_{2a\ell,exp}\mathbb{E}\left[\left(\int\_{0}^{\infty}e^{-K\_{f}s}|f\_{s}|\,ds\right)^{p}\right],\end{split} |  | (3.6) |

where N¬Į=‚ÄĖg‚ÄĖBMO\bar{N}=\|g\|\_{\text{BMO}}, q>1q>1 and a>0a>0 are two constants determined in the proof, and the function ūĚí¶\mathcal{K} is given in Lemma [3.3](#S3.Thmtheorem3 "Lemma 3.3 (Reverse H√∂lder inequality). ‚Ä£ 3.1 Preliminary lemmas ‚Ä£ 3 A general system of infinite horizon BSDEs with stochastic Lipschitz drivers ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies").
For ZmZ^{m} we have the following estimate:

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | ‚ÄĖZm‚ÄĖM2,K‚Ä≤2‚Č§c‚Äč‚ÄĖYm‚ÄĖ2,K2+c‚Äč‚ÄĖYm‚ÄĖ4,K2‚Äč(‚ÄĖg‚ÄĖBMO2+‚ÄĖŌē‚ÄĖBMO,KŌēr)+c‚Äč‚ÄĖYm‚ÄĖ2,K‚Äč‚ÄĖ|f|12‚ÄĖM4,Kf/22.\begin{split}\|Z^{m}\|^{2}\_{M^{2,K^{\prime}}}\leq~c\|Y^{m}\|^{2}\_{2,K}+c\|Y^{m}\|^{2}\_{4,K}\left(\|g\|^{2}\_{\text{BMO}}+\left\|\phi\right\|^{r}\_{\text{BMO},K\_{\phi}}\right)+c\|Y^{m}\|\_{2,K}\left\||f|^{\frac{1}{2}}\right\|^{2}\_{M^{4,K\_{f}/2}}.\end{split} |  | (3.7) |

If we further assume that |f|1/2‚ąąHBMO2,Kf/2|f|^{1/2}\in H^{2,K\_{f}/2}\_{\text{BMO}}, then (Ym,Zm)‚ąąL‚ąě,K√óHBMO2,K‚Ä≤(Y^{m},Z^{m})\in L^{\infty,K}\times H^{2,K^{\prime}}\_{\text{BMO}}. We also have the following estimate

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | ‚ÄĖYm‚ÄĖ‚ąě,K‚Č§c‚ÄčūĚí¶‚Äč(q,N¬Į)1q‚Äč‚ÄĖ|Ōē|r‚ÄĖ2‚Äča‚Äč‚Ąď,e‚Äčx‚Äčp12‚Äča‚Äč‚ÄĖ|f|12‚ÄĖBMO,12‚ÄčKf2,\begin{split}\|Y^{m}\|\_{\infty,K}\leq c\mathcal{K}(q,\bar{N})^{\frac{1}{q}}\left\||\phi|^{r}\right\|^{\frac{1}{2a}}\_{2a\ell,exp}\left\||f|^{\frac{1}{2}}\right\|^{2}\_{\text{BMO},\frac{1}{2}K\_{f}},\end{split} |  | (3.8) |

and

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | ‚ÄĖZm‚ÄĖBMO,K‚Ä≤2‚Č§c‚Äč‚ÄĖYm‚ÄĖ‚ąě,K2+c‚Äč‚ÄĖYm‚ÄĖ‚ąě,K2‚Äč(‚ÄĖg‚ÄĖBMO2+‚ÄĖŌē‚ÄĖBMO,KŌēr)+c‚Äč‚ÄĖ|f|12‚ÄĖBMO,12‚ÄčKf4.\begin{split}\|Z^{m}\|^{2}\_{\text{BMO},K^{\prime}}\leq&~c\|Y^{m}\|^{2}\_{\infty,K}+c\|Y^{m}\|^{2}\_{\infty,K}\left(\|g\|^{2}\_{\text{BMO}}+\left\|\phi\right\|^{r}\_{\text{BMO},K\_{\phi}}\right)+c\left\||f|^{\frac{1}{2}}\right\|^{4}\_{\text{BMO},\frac{1}{2}K\_{f}}.\end{split} |  | (3.9) |

###### Proof.

We first define Y~tm,i=e‚ąíK‚Äčt‚ÄčYtm,i\widetilde{Y}^{m,i}\_{t}=e^{-Kt}Y^{m,i}\_{t} and Z~tm,i=e‚ąíK‚Äčt‚ÄčZtm,i\widetilde{Z}^{m,i}\_{t}=e^{-Kt}Z^{m,i}\_{t}, which satisfy the following system of BSDEs:

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | {‚ąíd‚ÄčY~tm,i=[(K‚ąíőĹti)Y~tm,i+‚ąĎj=1‚Ąďqi‚ÄčjY~tm,j+‚ąĎj=1‚Ąďhm(őļti‚Äčj)Y~tm,j+hm(gti)‚ä§Z~tm,i+e‚ąíK‚Äčtfti]dt‚ąí(Z~tm,i)‚ä§dūĚí≤t,t‚ąą[0,m),Y~tm,i=0,t‚ąą[m,‚ąě),i‚ąą‚Ą≥.\left\{\begin{aligned} -d\widetilde{Y}^{m,i}\_{t}=&~\left[(K-\nu^{i}\_{t})\widetilde{Y}^{m,i}\_{t}+\sum^{\ell}\_{j=1}q^{ij}\widetilde{Y}^{m,j}\_{t}+\sum^{\ell}\_{j=1}h\_{m}(\kappa^{ij}\_{t})\widetilde{Y}^{m,j}\_{t}\right.\\ &~+h\_{m}(g^{i}\_{t})^{\top}\widetilde{Z}^{m,i}\_{t}+e^{-Kt}f^{i}\_{t}\Bigg]\,dt-(\widetilde{Z}^{m,i}\_{t})^{\top}\,d\mathcal{W}\_{t},\quad t\in[0,m),\\ \widetilde{Y}^{m,i}\_{t}=&~0,\quad t\in[m,\infty),\\ i\in&~\mathcal{M}.\end{aligned}\right. |  | (3.10) |

Due to the truncation, the system of BSDEs ([3.10](#S3.E10 "In Proof. ‚Ä£ 3.2 A general infinite-horizon BSDE system ‚Ä£ 3 A general system of infinite horizon BSDEs with stochastic Lipschitz drivers ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies")) admits a Lipschitz driver. As a result, the well-posedness of ([3.10](#S3.E10 "In Proof. ‚Ä£ 3.2 A general infinite-horizon BSDE system ‚Ä£ 3 A general system of infinite horizon BSDEs with stochastic Lipschitz drivers ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies"))‚ÄĒand hence of ([3.5](#S3.E5 "In 3.2 A general infinite-horizon BSDE system ‚Ä£ 3 A general system of infinite horizon BSDEs with stochastic Lipschitz drivers ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies"))‚ÄĒin the space S2,0√óM2,0S^{2,0}\times M^{2,0} follows from a standard result; see [[6](#bib.bib6), Theorem 4.1].

Next we verify that (Ym,Zm)‚ąą‚čāp‚Č•1Sp,K√óM2,K‚Ä≤(Y^{m},Z^{m})\in\bigcap\_{p\geq 1}S^{p,K}\times M^{2,K^{\prime}}. To this end, we introduce the following auxiliary system of BSDEs and compare its solution with that of ([3.10](#S3.E10 "In Proof. ‚Ä£ 3.2 A general infinite-horizon BSDE system ‚Ä£ 3 A general system of infinite horizon BSDEs with stochastic Lipschitz drivers ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies")):

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | {‚ąíd‚ÄčY¬Įtm,i=[‚ąĎj=1‚Ąďqi‚Äčj‚ÄčY¬Įtm,j+|őļt|‚Äč‚ąĎj=1‚ĄďY¬Įtm,j+|gt|‚Äč|Z¬Įtm,i|+e‚ąíK‚Äčt‚Äč|ft|]‚Äčd‚Äčt‚ąí(Z¬Įtm,i)‚ä§‚Äčd‚ÄčūĚí≤t,t‚ąą[0,m),Y¬Įtm,i=0,t‚ąą[m,‚ąě),i‚ąą‚Ą≥,\left\{\begin{aligned} -d\bar{Y}^{m,i}\_{t}=&~\left[\sum^{\ell}\_{j=1}q^{ij}\bar{Y}^{m,j}\_{t}+|\kappa\_{t}|\sum^{\ell}\_{j=1}\bar{Y}^{m,j}\_{t}+|g\_{t}||\bar{Z}^{m,i}\_{t}|+e^{-Kt}|f\_{t}|\right]\,dt-(\bar{Z}^{m,i}\_{t})^{\top}\,d\mathcal{W}\_{t},\quad t\in[0,m),\\ \bar{Y}^{m,i}\_{t}=&~0,\quad t\in[m,\infty),\\ i\in&~\cal M,\end{aligned}\right. |  | (3.11) |

where we have used the following notations of Euclidean norm

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  | |őļ|=(‚ąĎi,j=1‚Ąď|őļi‚Äčj|2)12,|g|=(‚ąĎi=1‚Ąď|gi|2)12,|f|=(‚ąĎi=1‚Ąď|fi|2)12.|\kappa|=\left(\sum^{\ell}\limits\_{i,j=1}|\kappa^{ij}|^{2}\right)^{\frac{1}{2}},\quad|g|=\left(\sum^{\ell}\limits\_{i=1}|g^{i}|^{2}\right)^{\frac{1}{2}},\quad|f|=\left(\sum^{\ell}\limits\_{i=1}|f^{i}|^{2}\right)^{\frac{1}{2}}. |  |

Step 1: the estimate for Y¬Įm,i\bar{Y}^{m,i}.
Indeed, any solution to the following one-dimensional BSDE is also a solution to the system ([3.11](#S3.E11 "In Proof. ‚Ä£ 3.2 A general infinite-horizon BSDE system ‚Ä£ 3 A general system of infinite horizon BSDEs with stochastic Lipschitz drivers ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies"))

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | {‚ąíd‚ÄčY¬Įtm=[‚Ąď‚Äč|őļt|‚ÄčY¬Įtm+(g~tm)‚ä§‚ÄčZ¬Įtm+e‚ąíK‚Äčt‚Äč|ft|]‚Äčd‚Äčt‚ąí(Z¬Įtm)‚ä§‚Äčd‚ÄčūĚí≤t,t‚ąą[0,m),Y¬Įtm=0,t‚ąą[m,‚ąě),\left\{\begin{aligned} -d\bar{Y}^{m}\_{t}=&~\left[\ell|\kappa\_{t}|\bar{Y}^{m}\_{t}+(\widetilde{g}\_{t}^{m})^{\top}\bar{Z}^{m}\_{t}+e^{-Kt}|f\_{t}|\right]\,dt-(\bar{Z}^{m}\_{t})^{\top}\,d\mathcal{W}\_{t},\quad t\in[0,m),\\ \bar{Y}^{m}\_{t}=&~0,\quad t\in[m,\infty),\end{aligned}\right. |  | (3.12) |

where g~tm:=|gt|‚ÄčZ¬Įtm|Z¬Įtm|‚ÄčūĚüŹ{|Z¬Įtm|‚Č†0}\widetilde{g}\_{t}^{m}:=|g\_{t}|\frac{\bar{Z}^{m}\_{t}}{|\bar{Z}^{m}\_{t}|}\mathbf{1}\_{\{|\bar{Z}^{m}\_{t}|\neq 0\}} for each tt. The explicit solution of ([3.12](#S3.E12 "In Proof. ‚Ä£ 3.2 A general infinite-horizon BSDE system ‚Ä£ 3 A general system of infinite horizon BSDEs with stochastic Lipschitz drivers ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies")) is given by (see e.g. [[24](#bib.bib24), Proposition 6.2.1])

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  | Y¬Įtm=(ő®tm)‚ąí1‚ÄčūĚĒľt‚Äč[‚ąętme‚ąíK‚Äčs‚Äčő®sm‚Äč|fs|‚ÄčūĚĎĎs]‚ÄčūĚüŹ{t‚Č§m}‚Č•0,\bar{Y}^{m}\_{t}=(\Psi\_{t}^{m})^{-1}\mathbb{E}\_{t}\left[\int^{m}\_{t}e^{-Ks}\Psi\_{s}^{m}|f\_{s}|\,ds\right]\mathbf{1}\_{\{t\leq m\}}\geq 0, |  |

where ő®m\Psi^{m} satisfies

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | ő®tm=‚Ąį‚Äč(g~m)t‚Äčőďt,with¬†‚Äčőďt:=exp‚Ā°{‚ąę0t‚Ąď‚Äč|őļs|‚ÄčūĚĎĎs}.\begin{split}\Psi^{m}\_{t}=\mathcal{E}(\widetilde{g}^{m})\_{t}\Gamma\_{t},\quad\text{with }\Gamma\_{t}:=\exp\left\{\int^{t}\_{0}\ell|\kappa\_{s}|\,ds\right\}.\end{split} |  | (3.13) |

By Assumption [3.4](#S3.Thmtheorem4 "Assumption 3.4. ‚Ä£ 3.2 A general infinite-horizon BSDE system ‚Ä£ 3 A general system of infinite horizon BSDEs with stochastic Lipschitz drivers ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies")(iv), we have |őļ|‚Č§|Ōē|r|\kappa|\leq|\phi|^{r}. Thus, for each p‚Č•1p\geq 1, applying Lemma [3.1](#S3.Thmtheorem1 "Lemma 3.1. ‚Ä£ 3.1 Preliminary lemmas ‚Ä£ 3 A general system of infinite horizon BSDEs with stochastic Lipschitz drivers ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies") with b1=rb\_{1}=r, b2=p‚Äč‚Ąďb\_{2}=p\ell, b3=0b\_{3}=0 and Kő∂=KŌē<0K\_{\zeta}=K\_{\phi}<0, we obtain

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | supŌĄūĚĒľŌĄ‚Äč[|őď‚ąěőďŌĄ|p]‚Č§supŌĄūĚĒľŌĄ‚Äč[ep‚Äč‚Ąď‚Äč‚ąęŌĄ‚ąě|Ōēs|r‚ÄčūĚĎĎs]‚Č§‚ÄĖ|Ōē|r‚ÄĖp‚Äč‚Ąď,e‚Äčx‚Äčp<‚ąě.\sup\_{\tau}\mathbb{E}\_{\tau}\left[\left|\frac{\Gamma\_{\infty}}{\Gamma\_{\tau}}\right|^{p}\right]\leq\sup\_{\tau}\mathbb{E}\_{\tau}\left[e^{p\ell\int^{\infty}\_{\tau}|\phi\_{s}|^{r}ds}\right]\leq\left\||\phi|^{r}\right\|\_{p\ell,exp}<\infty. |  | (3.14) |

Since |g~m|‚Č§|g||\widetilde{g}^{m}|\leq|g|, it follows that ‚ÄĖg~m‚ÄĖBMO,0<‚ąě\left\|\widetilde{g}^{m}\right\|\_{\text{BMO},0}<\infty. It implies that

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  | Nm:=‚ÄĖg~m‚ÄĖBMO,0‚Č§‚ÄĖg‚ÄĖBMO,0:=N¬Į.N^{m}:=\left\|\widetilde{g}^{m}\right\|\_{\text{BMO},0}\leq\left\|g\right\|\_{\text{BMO},0}:=\bar{N}. |  |

By [[16](#bib.bib16), Theorem 3.1], ‚Ąį‚Äč(g~m)\mathcal{E}(\widetilde{g}^{m}) satisfies the reverse H√∂lder inequality. Using Lemma [3.3](#S3.Thmtheorem3 "Lemma 3.3 (Reverse H√∂lder inequality). ‚Ä£ 3.1 Preliminary lemmas ‚Ä£ 3 A general system of infinite horizon BSDEs with stochastic Lipschitz drivers ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies"), for each 1<q<q‚ąó:=ő¶‚ąí1‚Äč(N¬Į)‚Č§ő¶‚ąí1‚Äč(Nm)1<q<q\_{\*}:=\Phi^{-1}(\bar{N})\leq\Phi^{-1}(N^{m}) and each ŌĄ‚ąąūĚíĮ\tau\in\mathcal{T}, it holds

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | ūĚĒľŌĄ‚Äč[|‚Ąį‚Äč(g~m)‚ąě‚Ąį‚Äč(g~m)ŌĄ|q]‚Č§ūĚí¶‚Äč(q,Nm)‚Č§ūĚí¶‚Äč(q,N¬Į).\mathbb{E}\_{\tau}\left[\left|\frac{\mathcal{E}(\widetilde{g}^{m})\_{\infty}}{\mathcal{E}(\widetilde{g}^{m})\_{\tau}}\right|^{q}\right]\leq\mathcal{K}(q,N^{m})\leq\mathcal{K}(q,\bar{N}). |  | (3.15) |

Let p‚ąóp\_{\*} be the conjugate exponent of q‚ąóq\_{\*}, and fix any a>p‚ąóa>p\_{\*} with the corresponding conjugate exponent qq. Then q<q‚ąóq<q\_{\*} and

inequality)‚Č§qq‚ąí1‚ÄčūĚĒľt‚Äč[|‚Ąį‚Äč(g~m)‚ąě‚Ąį‚Äč(g~m)t|q]1q‚ÄčūĚĒľt‚Äč[|őď‚ąěőďt|a‚Äč(‚ąęt‚ąěe‚ąíK‚Äčs‚Äč|fs|‚ÄčūĚĎĎs)a]1a(by conditional Doob‚Äôs maximal \leq&~\mathbb{E}\_{t}\left[\sup\_{u\geq t}\left|\frac{\Psi^{m}\_{u}}{\Psi^{m}\_{t}}\right|\int^{\infty}\_{t}e^{-Ks}|f\_{s}|\,ds\right]\\ =&~\mathbb{E}\_{t}\left[\sup\_{u\geq \eqref{eq:Psi-k}})\\ \leq&~\mathbb{E}\_{t}\left[\sup\_{u\geq H\"{o}lder's inequality})\\ \leq&~\frac{q}{q-1}\mathbb{E}\_{t}\left[\left|\frac{\mathcal{E}(\widetilde{g}^{m})\_{\infty}}{\mathcal{E}(\widetilde{g}^{m})\_{t}}\right|^{q}\right]^{\frac{1}{q}}\mathbb{E}\_{t}\left[\left|\frac{\Gamma\_{\infty}}{\Gamma\_{t}}\right|^{a}\left(\int^{\infty}\_{t}e^{-Ks}|f\_{s}|\,ds\right)^{a}\right]^{\frac{1}{a}}\quad(\text{by conditional Doob's maximal inequality})\\ \leq&~\frac{q}{q-1}\mathcal{K}(q,\bar{N})^{\frac{1}{q}}\mathbb{E}\_{t}\left[\left|\frac{\Gamma\_{\infty}}{\Gamma\_{t}}\right|^{2a}\right]^{\frac{1}{2a}}\mathbb{E}\_{t}\left[\left(\int^{\infty}\_{t}e^{-Ks}|f\_{s}|\,ds\right)^{2a}\right]^{\frac{1}{2a}}\quad(\text{by H\"{o}lder's inequality and \eqref{reverse}})\\ \leq&~\frac{q}{q-1}\mathcal{K}(q,\bar{N})^{\frac{1}{q}}\left\||\phi|^{r}\right\|^{\frac{1}{2a}}\_{2a\ell,exp}\mathbb{E}\_{t}\left[\left(\int\_{0}^{\infty}e^{-K\_{f}s}|f\_{s}|\,ds\right)^{2a}\right]^{\frac{1}{2a}}\quad(\text{by }\eqref{inequ:Gamma-k}\text{ and }K>K\_{f}).\end{split} |  | (3.16) |

Applying Doob‚Äôs maximal inequality, for any p>2‚Äčap>2a, we obtain

|  | ūĚĒľ‚Äč[supt‚Č•0(Y¬Įtm)p]‚Č§(qq‚ąí1)p‚ÄčūĚí¶‚Äč(q,N¬Į)pq‚Äč‚ÄĖ|Ōē|r‚ÄĖ2‚Äča‚Äč‚Ąď,e‚Äčx‚Äčpp2‚Äča‚ÄčūĚĒľ‚Äč[supt‚Č•0ūĚĒľt‚Äč[(‚ąę0‚ąěe‚ąíKf‚Äčs‚Äč|fs|‚ÄčūĚĎĎs)2‚Äča]p2‚Äča]‚Č§(qq‚ąí1)p‚Äč(pp‚ąí2‚Äča)p2‚Äča‚ÄčūĚí¶‚Äč(q,N¬Į)pq‚Äč‚ÄĖ|Ōē|r‚ÄĖ2‚Äča‚Äč‚Ąď,e‚Äčx‚Äčpp2‚Äča‚ÄčūĚĒľ‚Äč[(‚ąę0‚ąěe‚ąíKf‚Äčs‚Äč|fs|‚ÄčūĚĎĎs)p].\begin{split}\mathbb{E}\left[\sup\_{t\geq 0}(\bar{Y}^{m}\_{t})^{p}\right]\leq&~\left(\frac{q}{q-1}\right)^{p}\mathcal{K}(q,\bar{N})^{\frac{p}{q}}\left\||\phi|^{r}\right\|^{\frac{p}{2a}}\_{2a\ell,exp}\mathbb{E}\left[\sup\_{t\geq 0}\mathbb{E}\_{t}\left[\left(\int\_{0}^{\infty}e^{-K\_{f}s}|f\_{s}|\,ds\right)^{2a}\right]^{\frac{p}{2a}}\right]\\ \leq&~\left(\frac{q}{q-1}\right)^{p}\left(\frac{p}{p-2a}\right)^{\frac{p}{2a}}\mathcal{K}(q,\bar{N})^{\frac{p}{q}}\left\||\phi|^{r}\right\|^{\frac{p}{2a}}\_{2a\ell,exp}\mathbb{E}\left[\left(\int\_{0}^{\infty}e^{-K\_{f}s}|f\_{s}|\,ds\right)^{p}\right].\end{split} |  |

Step 2: the estimate for Y~m,i\widetilde{Y}^{m,i} and Ym,iY^{m,i}.
The system of BSDEs ([3.10](#S3.E10 "In Proof. ‚Ä£ 3.2 A general infinite-horizon BSDE system ‚Ä£ 3 A general system of infinite horizon BSDEs with stochastic Lipschitz drivers ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies")) satisfies all the conditions of [[12](#bib.bib12), Lemma 2.2] (see also [[13](#bib.bib13)]). In particular, the inequality (K‚ąíőĹti)‚ÄčY¬Įtm‚Č§0(K-\nu^{i}\_{t})\bar{Y}^{m}\_{t}\leq 0 holds under the assumption K<K¬ĮK<\bar{K} and Assumption¬†[3.4](#S3.Thmtheorem4 "Assumption 3.4. ‚Ä£ 3.2 A general infinite-horizon BSDE system ‚Ä£ 3 A general system of infinite horizon BSDEs with stochastic Lipschitz drivers ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies")(v). This implies that

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  | (K‚ąíőĹti)‚ÄčY¬Įtm+‚ąĎj=1‚Ąďqi‚Äčj‚ÄčY¬Įtm+‚ąĎj=1‚Ąďhm‚Äč(őļti‚Äčj)‚ÄčY¬Įtm‚Č§‚Ąď‚Äč|őļt|‚ÄčY¬Įtm.(K-\nu^{i}\_{t})\bar{Y}^{m}\_{t}+\sum^{\ell}\_{j=1}q^{ij}\bar{Y}^{m}\_{t}+\sum^{\ell}\_{j=1}h\_{m}(\kappa^{ij}\_{t})\bar{Y}^{m}\_{t}\leq\ell|\kappa\_{t}|\bar{Y}^{m}\_{t}. |  |

Moreover, by the definitions of g~m\widetilde{g}^{m} and hmh\_{m}, we have

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  | hm‚Äč(gti)‚ä§‚ÄčZ¬Įtm‚Č§(g~tm)‚ä§‚ÄčZ¬Įtm‚Äč¬†for¬†‚Äči‚ąą‚Ą≥.h\_{m}(g^{i}\_{t})^{\top}\bar{Z}^{m}\_{t}\leq(\widetilde{g}\_{t}^{m})^{\top}\bar{Z}^{m}\_{t}\text{ for }i\in\cal M. |  |

Thus, Condition (iv) in [[12](#bib.bib12)] is satisfied. The driver of ([3.10](#S3.E10 "In Proof. ‚Ä£ 3.2 A general infinite-horizon BSDE system ‚Ä£ 3 A general system of infinite horizon BSDEs with stochastic Lipschitz drivers ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies")) satisfies Condition (iii) in [[12](#bib.bib12)], because qi‚Äčj‚Č•0q^{ij}\geq 0 and őļi‚Äčj‚Č•0\kappa^{ij}\geq 0. Conditions (i) and (ii) are satisfied trivially.
Therefore, by applying [[12](#bib.bib12), Lemma 2.2], we conclude that for each i=1,‚čĮ,‚Ąďi=1,\cdots,\ell,

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | |Y~tm,i|‚Č§Y¬Įt.|\widetilde{Y}^{m,i}\_{t}|\leq\bar{Y}\_{t}. |  | (3.17) |

As a result, the estimate ([3.6](#S3.E6 "In Lemma 3.5. ‚Ä£ 3.2 A general infinite-horizon BSDE system ‚Ä£ 3 A general system of infinite horizon BSDEs with stochastic Lipschitz drivers ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies")) follows.

By the assumption that K‚Ä≤>K>KfK^{\prime}>K>K\_{f} and the fact that |Ztm,i|=0|Z^{m,i}\_{t}|=0 for t‚ąą(m,‚ąě)t\in(m,\infty), we get that

| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | ūĚĒľŌĄ‚Äč[‚ąęŌĄ‚ąěe‚ąí2‚ÄčK‚Ä≤‚Äčs‚Äč|Zsm|2‚ÄčūĚĎĎs]‚Č§c‚ÄčūĚĒľŌĄ‚Äč[supt‚Č•ŌĄe‚ąí2‚ÄčK‚Äčt‚Äč|Ytm|2]+c‚ÄčūĚĒľŌĄ‚Äč[supt‚Č•ŌĄe‚ąí4‚ÄčK‚Äčt‚Äč|Ytm|4]1/2‚ÄčūĚĒľŌĄ‚Äč[(‚ąęŌĄ‚ąě|gs|2‚ÄčūĚĎĎs)2]1/2+c‚ÄčūĚĒľŌĄ‚Äč[supt‚Č•ŌĄe‚ąí4‚ÄčK‚Äčt‚Äč|Ytm|4]1/2‚ÄčūĚĒľŌĄ‚Äč[(‚ąęŌĄ‚ąě|Ōēs|2‚ÄčūĚĎĎs)r]1/2+c‚ÄčūĚĒľŌĄ‚Äč[supt‚Č•ŌĄe‚ąí2‚ÄčK‚Äčt‚Äč|Ytm|2]1/2‚ÄčūĚĒľŌĄ‚Äč[(‚ąęŌĄ‚ąěe‚ąíKf‚Äčs‚Äč|fs|‚ÄčūĚĎĎs)2]1/2,\begin{split}\mathbb{E}\_{\tau}\left[\int^{\infty}\_{\tau}e^{-2K^{\prime}s}|Z^{m}\_{s}|^{2}\,ds\right]\leq&~c\mathbb{E}\_{\tau}\left[\sup\_{t\geq{\tau}}e^{-2Kt}|Y\_{t}^{m}|^{2}\right]+c\mathbb{E}\_{\tau}\left[\sup\_{t\geq{\tau}}e^{-4Kt}|Y\_{t}^{m}|^{4}\right]^{1/2}\mathbb{E}\_{\tau}\left[\left(\int\_{\tau}^{\infty}|g\_{s}|^{2}\,ds\right)^{2}\right]^{1/2}\\ &~+c\mathbb{E}\_{\tau}\left[\sup\_{t\geq{\tau}}e^{-4Kt}|Y^{m}\_{t}|^{4}\right]^{1/2}\mathbb{E}\_{\tau}\left[\left(\int\_{\tau}^{\infty}|\phi\_{s}|^{2}\,ds\right)^{r}\right]^{1/2}\\ &~+c\mathbb{E}\_{\tau}\left[\sup\_{t\geq{\tau}}e^{-2Kt}|Y\_{t}^{m}|^{2}\right]^{1/2}\mathbb{E}\_{\tau}\left[\left(\int\_{\tau}^{\infty}e^{-K\_{f}s}|f\_{s}|\,ds\right)^{2}\right]^{1/2},\end{split} |  | (3.18) |

from which we obtain the estimate ([3.7](#S3.E7 "In Lemma 3.5. ‚Ä£ 3.2 A general infinite-horizon BSDE system ‚Ä£ 3 A general system of infinite horizon BSDEs with stochastic Lipschitz drivers ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies")) for ŌĄ=0\tau=0.

If we further assume that |f|1/2‚ąąHBMO2,Kf/2|f|^{1/2}\in H^{2,K\_{f}/2}\_{\text{BMO}}, then by ([3.16](#S3.E16 "In Proof. ‚Ä£ 3.2 A general infinite-horizon BSDE system ‚Ä£ 3 A general system of infinite horizon BSDEs with stochastic Lipschitz drivers ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies"))-([3.18](#S3.E18 "In Proof. ‚Ä£ 3.2 A general infinite-horizon BSDE system ‚Ä£ 3 A general system of infinite horizon BSDEs with stochastic Lipschitz drivers ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies")) together with Lemma [3.2](#S3.Thmtheorem2 "Lemma 3.2 (Energy inequality). ‚Ä£ 3.1 Preliminary lemmas ‚Ä£ 3 A general system of infinite horizon BSDEs with stochastic Lipschitz drivers ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies"), we can easily obtain the desired estimates ([3.8](#S3.E8 "In Lemma 3.5. ‚Ä£ 3.2 A general infinite-horizon BSDE system ‚Ä£ 3 A general system of infinite horizon BSDEs with stochastic Lipschitz drivers ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies")) and ([3.9](#S3.E9 "In Lemma 3.5. ‚Ä£ 3.2 A general infinite-horizon BSDE system ‚Ä£ 3 A general system of infinite horizon BSDEs with stochastic Lipschitz drivers ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies")).
‚ąé

###### Remark 3.6.

By a similar argument as in Step 3, we can also obtain the following estimate for ZmZ^{m} for each p‚Č•1p\geq 1

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | ūĚĒľ‚Äč[(‚ąę0‚ąěe‚ąí2‚ÄčK‚Ä≤‚Äčs‚Äč|Zsm|2‚ÄčūĚĎĎs)p]‚Č§c‚ÄčūĚĒľ‚Äč[supt‚Č•0e‚ąí2‚Äčp‚ÄčK‚Äčt‚Äč|Ytm|2‚Äčp]+c‚ÄčūĚĒľ‚Äč[supt‚Č•0e‚ąí4‚Äčp‚ÄčK‚Äčt‚Äč|Ytm|4‚Äčp]1/2‚ÄčūĚĒľ‚Äč[(‚ąę0‚ąě|gs|2‚ÄčūĚĎĎs)2‚Äčp]1/2+c‚ÄčūĚĒľ‚Äč[supt‚Č•0e‚ąí4‚Äčp‚ÄčK‚Äčt‚Äč|Ytm|4‚Äčp]1/2‚ÄčūĚĒľ‚Äč[(‚ąę0‚ąě|Ōēs|2‚ÄčūĚĎĎs)r‚Äčp]1/2+c‚ÄčūĚĒľ‚Äč[supt‚Č•0e‚ąí2‚Äčp‚ÄčK‚Äčt‚Äč|Ytm|2‚Äčp]1/2‚ÄčūĚĒľ‚Äč[(‚ąę0‚ąěe‚ąíKf‚Äčs‚Äč|fs|‚ÄčūĚĎĎs)2‚Äčp]1/2.\begin{split}&~\mathbb{E}\left[\left(\int^{\infty}\_{0}e^{-2K^{\prime}s}|Z^{m}\_{s}|^{2}\,ds\right)^{p}\right]\\ \leq&~c\mathbb{E}\left[\sup\_{t\geq 0}e^{-2pKt}|Y\_{t}^{m}|^{2p}\right]+c\mathbb{E}\left[\sup\_{t\geq 0}e^{-4pKt}|Y\_{t}^{m}|^{4p}\right]^{1/2}\mathbb{E}\left[\left(\int\_{0}^{\infty}|g\_{s}|^{2}\,ds\right)^{2p}\right]^{1/2}\\ &~+c\mathbb{E}\left[\sup\_{t\geq 0}e^{-4pKt}|Y^{m}\_{t}|^{4p}\right]^{1/2}\mathbb{E}\left[\left(\int\_{0}^{\infty}|\phi\_{s}|^{2}\,ds\right)^{rp}\right]^{1/2}\\ &~+c\mathbb{E}\left[\sup\_{t\geq 0}e^{-2pKt}|Y\_{t}^{m}|^{2p}\right]^{1/2}\mathbb{E}\left[\left(\int\_{0}^{\infty}e^{-K\_{f}s}|f\_{s}|\,ds\right)^{2p}\right]^{1/2}.\end{split} |  | (3.19) |

This estimate will be used in the proof of Theorem [3.7](#S3.Thmtheorem7 "Theorem 3.7. ‚Ä£ 3.2 A general infinite-horizon BSDE system ‚Ä£ 3 A general system of infinite horizon BSDEs with stochastic Lipschitz drivers ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies").

###### Theorem 3.7.

For any given KYK\_{Y} and KZK\_{Z} satisfying Kf<KY<KZ<K¬ĮK\_{f}<K\_{Y}<K\_{Z}<\bar{K}, the system of BSDEs ([3.4](#S3.E4 "In 3.2 A general infinite-horizon BSDE system ‚Ä£ 3 A general system of infinite horizon BSDEs with stochastic Lipschitz drivers ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies")) admits a solution (Y,Z)(Y,Z) in ‚čāp‚Č•1Sp,KY√óM2,KZ\bigcap\_{p\geq 1}S^{p,K\_{Y}}\times M^{2,K\_{Z}}, satisfying the following transversality condition

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | limT‚Üí‚ąěūĚĒľ‚Äč[e‚ąíp‚ÄčKY‚ÄčT‚Äč|YT|p]=0.\begin{split}\lim\_{T\rightarrow\infty}\mathbb{E}\left[e^{-pK\_{Y}T}|Y\_{T}|^{p}\right]=0.\end{split} |  | (3.20) |

If we further assume that |f|1/2‚ąąHBMO2,Kf/2|f|^{1/2}\in H^{2,K\_{f}/2}\_{\text{BMO}}, the solution (Y,Z)(Y,Z) belongs to a finer space L‚ąě,KY√óHBMO2,KZL^{\infty,K\_{Y}}\times H^{2,K\_{Z}}\_{\text{BMO}}.

###### Proof.

Given KYK\_{Y} and KZK\_{Z} as in the statement of the theorem, choose constants KFK\_{F}, KK and K‚Ä≤K^{\prime} such that

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  | Kf<K<K‚Ä≤<KF<KY<K¬Į.K\_{f}<K<K^{\prime}<K\_{F}<K\_{Y}<\bar{K}. |  |

For any m1,m2‚ąą‚Ąēm\_{1},m\_{2}\in\mathbb{N}, denote by (Ym2,Zm2)(Y^{m\_{2}},Z^{m\_{2}}) and (Ym1,Zm1)‚ąąL‚ąě,K√óHBMO2,K‚Ä≤(Y^{m\_{1}},Z^{m\_{1}})\in L^{\infty,K}\times H^{2,K^{\prime}}\_{\text{BMO}} the solutions to the BSDE ([3.5](#S3.E5 "In 3.2 A general infinite-horizon BSDE system ‚Ä£ 3 A general system of infinite horizon BSDEs with stochastic Lipschitz drivers ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies")) with m=m2m=m\_{2} and m=m1m=m\_{1}, respectively, as constructed in Lemma¬†[3.5](#S3.Thmtheorem5 "Lemma 3.5. ‚Ä£ 3.2 A general infinite-horizon BSDE system ‚Ä£ 3 A general system of infinite horizon BSDEs with stochastic Lipschitz drivers ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies"). Define the difference processes

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  | (őĒ‚ÄčY‚Äč(m2,m1),őĒ‚ÄčZ‚Äč(m2,m1)):=(Ym2‚ąíYm1,Zm2‚ąíZm1).\left(\Delta Y(m\_{2},m\_{1}),\ \Delta Z(m\_{2},m\_{1})\right):=\left(Y^{m\_{2}}-Y^{m\_{1}},\ Z^{m\_{2}}-Z^{m\_{1}}\right). |  |

Then (őĒ‚ÄčY‚Äč(m2,m1),őĒ‚ÄčZ‚Äč(m2,m1))\left(\Delta Y(m\_{2},m\_{1}),\ \Delta Z(m\_{2},m\_{1})\right) satisfies the BSDE system ([3.5](#S3.E5 "In 3.2 A general infinite-horizon BSDE system ‚Ä£ 3 A general system of infinite horizon BSDEs with stochastic Lipschitz drivers ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies")) with m=m2m=m\_{2} and fif^{i} replaced by

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  | Fsi‚Äč(m2,m1):=(hm2‚Äč(gsi)‚ąíhm1‚Äč(gsi))‚ä§‚ÄčZsm2,i+‚ąĎj=1‚Ąď(hm2‚Äč(őļsi‚Äčj)‚ąíhm1‚Äč(őļsi‚Äčj))‚ÄčYsm2,j+fsi‚Äč1[m1,m2).F^{i}\_{s}(m\_{2},m\_{1}):=\left(h\_{m\_{2}}(g^{i}\_{s})-h\_{m\_{1}}(g^{i}\_{s})\right)^{\top}Z^{m\_{2},i}\_{s}+\sum\_{j=1}^{\ell}\left(h\_{m\_{2}}(\kappa^{ij}\_{s})-h\_{m\_{1}}(\kappa^{ij}\_{s})\right)Y^{m\_{2},j}\_{s}+f^{i}\_{s}\textbf{1}\_{[m\_{1},m\_{2})}. |  |

Step 1: the estimate and convergence of FiF^{i}. In this step, we verify FiF^{i} satisfies Assumption [3.4](#S3.Thmtheorem4 "Assumption 3.4. ‚Ä£ 3.2 A general infinite-horizon BSDE system ‚Ä£ 3 A general system of infinite horizon BSDEs with stochastic Lipschitz drivers ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies")(ii) for the constant KFK\_{F}.

By H√∂lder‚Äôs inequality we have the following convergence estimate for each p‚Č•1p\geq 1:

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | ūĚĒľ‚Äč[(‚ąę0‚ąěe‚ąíKF‚Äčs‚Äč|Fsi‚Äč(m2,m1)|‚ÄčūĚĎĎs)p]‚Č§c‚Äčsupi‚ąą‚Ą≥ūĚĒľ‚Äč[(‚ąę0‚ąě|hm2‚Äč(gsi)‚ąíhm1‚Äč(gsi)|2‚ÄčūĚĎĎs)p]12‚ÄčūĚĒľ‚Äč[(‚ąę0‚ąěe‚ąí2‚ÄčK‚Ä≤‚Äčs‚Äč|Zsm2,i|2‚ÄčūĚĎĎs)p]12+c‚ÄčūĚĒľ‚Äč[supt‚Č•0e‚ąí2‚Äčp‚ÄčK‚Äčt‚Äč|Ytm|2‚Äčp]1/2‚ÄčūĚĒľ‚Äč[(‚ąę0‚ąěe‚ąí(KF‚ąíK)‚Äčs‚Äč|hm2‚Äč(őļsi‚Äčj)‚ąíhm1‚Äč(őļsi‚Äčj)|‚ÄčūĚĎĎs)2‚Äčp]12+c‚ÄčūĚĒľ‚Äč[(‚ąę0‚ąěe‚ąíKf‚Äčs‚Äč|fsi‚Äč1[m1,m2)|‚ÄčūĚĎĎs)p]‚Üí0,¬†as¬†‚Äčm2,m1‚Üí‚ąě.\begin{split}&~\mathbb{E}\left[\left(\int\_{0}^{\infty}e^{-K\_{F}s}|F^{i}\_{s}(m\_{2},m\_{1})|\,ds\right)^{p}\right]\\ \leq&~c\sup\_{i\in\cal M}\mathbb{E}\left[\left(\int^{\infty}\_{0}|h\_{m\_{2}}(g^{i}\_{s})-h\_{m\_{1}}(g^{i}\_{s})|^{2}\,ds\right)^{p}\right]^{\frac{1}{2}}\mathbb{E}\left[\left(\int^{\infty}\_{0}e^{-2K^{\prime}s}|Z^{m\_{2},i}\_{s}|^{2}\,ds\right)^{p}\right]^{\frac{1}{2}}\\ &~+c\mathbb{E}\left[\sup\_{t\geq 0}e^{-2pKt}|Y\_{t}^{m}|^{2p}\right]^{1/2}\mathbb{E}\left[\left(\int^{\infty}\_{0}e^{-(K\_{F}-K)s}|h\_{m\_{2}}(\kappa^{ij}\_{s})-h\_{m\_{1}}(\kappa^{ij}\_{s})|\,ds\right)^{2p}\right]^{\frac{1}{2}}\\ &~+c\mathbb{E}\left[\left(\int^{\infty}\_{0}e^{-K\_{f}s}|f^{i}\_{s}\textbf{1}\_{[m\_{1},m\_{2})}|\,ds\right)^{p}\right]\\ {\rightarrow}&~0,\qquad\text{ as }{m\_{2},m\_{1}\to\infty}.\end{split} |  | (3.21) |

This convergence follows from the following two facts:

* i).

  The uniform bounds hold:

  |  |  |  |
  | --- | --- | --- |
  |  | supm‚ÄĖYm‚ÄĖ2‚Äčp,K‚Äč<‚ąě,and‚Äčsupm‚ą•‚ÄčZm,i‚ą•M2‚Äčp,K‚Ä≤<‚ąě\sup\_{m}\|Y^{m}\|\_{2p,K}<\infty,\quad\text{and}\sup\_{m}\left\|Z^{m,i}\right\|\_{M^{2p,K^{\prime}}}<\infty |  |

  by estimates ([3.6](#S3.E6 "In Lemma 3.5. ‚Ä£ 3.2 A general infinite-horizon BSDE system ‚Ä£ 3 A general system of infinite horizon BSDEs with stochastic Lipschitz drivers ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies")) and ([3.19](#S3.E19 "In Remark 3.6. ‚Ä£ 3.2 A general infinite-horizon BSDE system ‚Ä£ 3 A general system of infinite horizon BSDEs with stochastic Lipschitz drivers ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies")).
* ii).

  The truncation error vanishes as m‚Üí‚ąěm\to\infty: for example,

  |  |  |  |
  | --- | --- | --- |
  |  | ūĚĒľ‚Äč[(‚ąę0‚ąě|hm‚Äč(gsi)‚ąígsi|2‚ÄčūĚĎĎs)p]=ūĚĒľ‚Äč[(‚ąę0‚ąě|m|gsi|‚Äčgsi‚ÄčūĚüŹ{|gsi|‚Č•m}+gsi‚ÄčūĚüŹ{0<|gsi|<m}‚ąígsi|2‚ÄčūĚĎĎs)p]‚Č§22‚Äčp+1‚ÄčūĚĒľ‚Äč[(‚ąę0‚ąě|gsi|2‚ÄčūĚüŹ{|gsi|‚Č•m}‚ÄčūĚĎĎs)p]‚Üí0,\begin{split}&~\mathbb{E}\left[\left(\int^{\infty}\_{0}|h\_{m}(g^{i}\_{s})-g^{i}\_{s}|^{2}\,ds\right)^{p}\right]\\ =&~\mathbb{E}\left[\left(\int^{\infty}\_{0}\left|\frac{m}{|g^{i}\_{s}|}g^{i}\_{s}\mathbf{1}\_{\{|g^{i}\_{s}|\geq m\}}+g^{i}\_{s}\mathbf{1}\_{\{0<|g^{i}\_{s}|<m\}}-g^{i}\_{s}\right|^{2}\,ds\right)^{p}\right]\\ \leq&~2^{2p+1}\mathbb{E}\left[\left(\int\_{0}^{\infty}|g^{i}\_{s}|^{2}\mathbf{1}\_{\{|g^{i}\_{s}|\geq m\}}\,ds\right)^{p}\right]\\ \rightarrow&~0,\end{split} |  |

  by Assumption [3.4](#S3.Thmtheorem4 "Assumption 3.4. ‚Ä£ 3.2 A general infinite-horizon BSDE system ‚Ä£ 3 A general system of infinite horizon BSDEs with stochastic Lipschitz drivers ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies")(ii). A similar argument applies to hm‚Äč(őļ),f‚Äč1[0,m)h\_{m}(\kappa),f\textbf{1}\_{[0,m)}.

Step 2: convergence of őĒ‚ÄčYi\Delta Y^{i} and őĒ‚ÄčZi\Delta Z^{i}. By Lemma [3.5](#S3.Thmtheorem5 "Lemma 3.5. ‚Ä£ 3.2 A general infinite-horizon BSDE system ‚Ä£ 3 A general system of infinite horizon BSDEs with stochastic Lipschitz drivers ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies"), (őĒ‚ÄčY,őĒ‚ÄčZ)‚ąą‚čāp‚Č•1Sp,KY√óM2,KZ(\Delta Y,\Delta Z)\in\bigcap\_{p\geq 1}S^{p,K\_{Y}}\times M^{2,K\_{Z}}. In this step, we consider the convergence of the difference process.

By ([3.6](#S3.E6 "In Lemma 3.5. ‚Ä£ 3.2 A general infinite-horizon BSDE system ‚Ä£ 3 A general system of infinite horizon BSDEs with stochastic Lipschitz drivers ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies")) in Lemma [3.5](#S3.Thmtheorem5 "Lemma 3.5. ‚Ä£ 3.2 A general infinite-horizon BSDE system ‚Ä£ 3 A general system of infinite horizon BSDEs with stochastic Lipschitz drivers ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies") and the convergence ([3.21](#S3.E21 "In Proof. ‚Ä£ 3.2 A general infinite-horizon BSDE system ‚Ä£ 3 A general system of infinite horizon BSDEs with stochastic Lipschitz drivers ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies")), we obtain for any p>2‚Äčap>2a

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | ūĚĒľ‚Äč[supt‚Č•0|e‚ąíKY‚Äčt‚ÄčőĒ‚ÄčYti‚Äč(m2,m1)|p]‚Č§(qq‚ąí1)p‚Äč(pp‚ąí2‚Äča)p2‚Äča‚ÄčūĚí¶‚Äč(q,N¬Į)pq‚Äč‚ÄĖ|Ōēs|r‚ÄĖ2‚Äča‚Äč‚Ąď,e‚Äčx‚Äčpp2‚Äča‚ÄčūĚĒľ‚Äč[(‚ąę0‚ąěe‚ąíKF‚Äčs‚Äč|Fs‚Äč(m2,m1)|‚ÄčūĚĎĎs)p]‚Üí0,as¬†‚Äčm2‚Äč¬†and¬†‚Äčm1‚Üí‚ąě.\begin{split}&~\mathbb{E}\left[\sup\_{t\geq 0}\left|e^{-K\_{Y}t}\Delta Y^{i}\_{t}(m\_{2},m\_{1})\right|^{p}\right]\\ \leq&~\left(\frac{q}{q-1}\right)^{p}\left(\frac{p}{p-2a}\right)^{\frac{p}{2a}}\mathcal{K}(q,\bar{N})^{\frac{p}{q}}\left\||\phi\_{s}|^{r}\right\|^{\frac{p}{2a}}\_{2a\ell,exp}\mathbb{E}\left[\left(\int\_{0}^{\infty}e^{-K\_{F}s}|F\_{s}(m\_{2},m\_{1})|\,ds\right)^{p}\right]\\ \rightarrow&~0,\quad\text{as }m\_{2}\text{ and }m\_{1}\rightarrow\infty.\end{split} |  | (3.22) |

By the estimate ([3.7](#S3.E7 "In Lemma 3.5. ‚Ä£ 3.2 A general infinite-horizon BSDE system ‚Ä£ 3 A general system of infinite horizon BSDEs with stochastic Lipschitz drivers ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies")), we have

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | ūĚĒľ‚Äč[‚ąę0‚ąěe‚ąí2‚ÄčKZ‚Äčs‚Äč|őĒ‚ÄčZs‚Äč(m2,m1)|2‚ÄčūĚĎĎs]‚Č§c‚ÄčūĚĒľ‚Äč[supt‚Č•0e‚ąí2‚ÄčKY‚Äčt‚Äč|őĒ‚ÄčYt‚Äč(m2,m1)|2]+c‚ÄčūĚĒľ‚Äč[supt‚Č•0|e‚ąíKY‚Äčt‚ÄčőĒ‚ÄčYt‚Äč(m2,m1)|4]1/2‚ÄčūĚĒľ‚Äč[(‚ąę0‚ąě|gs|2‚ÄčūĚĎĎs)2]1/2+c‚ÄčūĚĒľ‚Äč[supt‚Č•0|e‚ąíKY‚Äčt‚ÄčőĒ‚ÄčYt‚Äč(m2,m1)|4]1/2‚ÄčūĚĒľ‚Äč[(‚ąę0‚ąě|Ōēs|2‚ÄčūĚĎĎs)r]1/2+c‚ÄčūĚĒľ‚Äč[supt‚Č•0|e‚ąíKY‚Äčt‚ÄčőĒ‚ÄčYt‚Äč(m2,m1)|2]1/2‚ÄčūĚĒľ‚Äč[(‚ąę0‚ąěe‚ąíKF‚Äčs‚Äč|Fs|‚ÄčūĚĎĎs)2]1/2‚Üím2,m1‚Üí‚ąě0.\begin{split}&~\mathbb{E}\left[\int\_{0}^{\infty}e^{-2K\_{Z}s}|\Delta Z\_{s}(m\_{2},m\_{1})|^{2}\,ds\right]\\ \leq&~c\mathbb{E}\left[\sup\_{t\geq 0}e^{-2K\_{Y}t}|\Delta Y\_{t}(m\_{2},m\_{1})|^{2}\right]+c\mathbb{E}\left[\sup\_{t\geq 0}|e^{-K\_{Y}t}\Delta Y\_{t}(m\_{2},m\_{1})|^{4}\right]^{1/2}\mathbb{E}\left[\left(\int\_{0}^{\infty}|g\_{s}|^{2}\,ds\right)^{2}\right]^{1/2}\\ &~+c\mathbb{E}\left[\sup\_{t\geq 0}|e^{-K\_{Y}t}\Delta Y\_{t}(m\_{2},m\_{1})|^{4}\right]^{1/2}\mathbb{E}\left[\left(\int\_{0}^{\infty}|\phi\_{s}|^{2}\,ds\right)^{r}\right]^{1/2}\\ &~+c\mathbb{E}\left[\sup\_{t\geq 0}|e^{-K\_{Y}t}\Delta Y\_{t}(m\_{2},m\_{1})|^{2}\right]^{1/2}\mathbb{E}\left[\left(\int\_{0}^{\infty}e^{-K\_{F}s}|F\_{s}|\,ds\right)^{2}\right]^{1/2}\\ &\xrightarrow{m\_{2},m\_{1}\to\infty}0.\end{split} |  | (3.23) |

Thus, the sequence (Ym,Zm)(Y^{m},Z^{m}) is a Cauchy one in ‚čāp‚Č•1Sp,KY√óM2,KZ\bigcap\_{p\geq 1}S^{p,K\_{Y}}\times M^{2,K\_{Z}}, and admits a limit denoted by (Y,Z)‚ąą‚čāp‚Č•1Sp,KY√óM2,KZ(Y,Z)\in\bigcap\_{p\geq 1}S^{p,K\_{Y}}\times M^{2,K\_{Z}}.

by the convergence in Step 2.

### 3.3 The BSDE Systems ([2.4](#S2.E4 "In 2 Candidate BSDE systems ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies"))-([2.9](#S2.E9 "In 2 Candidate BSDE systems ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies")): Existence

In this section, we establish the existence of solutions to the infinite-horizon BSDE systems ([2.4](#S2.E4 "In 2 Candidate BSDE systems ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies"))‚Äď([2.9](#S2.E9 "In 2 Candidate BSDE systems ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies")). Among these, the system for AA, given by ([2.4](#S2.E4 "In 2 Candidate BSDE systems ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies"))‚Äď([2.5](#S2.E5 "In 2 Candidate BSDE systems ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies")), can be treated by adapting the argument in [[14](#bib.bib14), Theorem 4.2]; the relevant results are summarized in Appendix [A](#A1 "Appendix A Results on ūĚźī. ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies"). The existence results for the systems corresponding to BB and CC will be established using the framework developed in Section¬†[3.2](#S3.SS2 "3.2 A general infinite-horizon BSDE system ‚Ä£ 3 A general system of infinite horizon BSDEs with stochastic Lipschitz drivers ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies").

The following estimate for 1ő≥\frac{1}{\gamma} will be used frequently.

###### Lemma 3.8.

Under Assumption [1.1](#S1.Thmtheorem1 "Assumption 1.1. ‚Ä£ 1.1 Notation, convention, assumption and admissible space ‚Ä£ 1 Introduction ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies"), for each p‚Č•1p\geq 1, we have

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  | ūĚĒľ‚Äč[supt‚Č•0|1ő≥t|p]<‚ąě.\mathbb{E}\left[\sup\_{t\geq 0}\left|\frac{1}{\gamma\_{t}}\right|^{p}\right]<\infty. |  |

###### Proof.

From ([1.3](#S1.E3 "In 1 Introduction ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies")) we have

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  | d‚Äč1ő≥s=1ő≥s‚Äč((‚ąíőľs+ŌÉ1,s2)‚Äčd‚Äčs‚ąíŌÉ1,s‚Äčd‚ÄčWs),d\frac{1}{\gamma\_{s}}=\frac{1}{\gamma\_{s}}\Bigg(\left(-\mu\_{s}+\sigma\_{1,s}^{2}\right)\,ds-\sigma\_{1,s}\,dW\_{s}\Bigg), |  |

which implies the closed form expression

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  | 1ő≥t=1ő≥0‚Äčexp‚Ā°{‚ąę0t(‚ąíőľs+ŌÉ1,s22)‚ÄčūĚĎĎs‚ąí‚ąę0tŌÉ1,s‚ÄčūĚĎĎWs}.\frac{1}{\gamma\_{t}}=\frac{1}{\gamma\_{0}}\exp\left\{\int^{t}\_{0}\left(-\mu\_{s}+\frac{\sigma\_{1,s}^{2}}{2}\right)\,ds-\int^{t}\_{0}\sigma\_{1,s}\,dW\_{s}\right\}. |  |

Since |őľt|‚Č§c^‚Äče‚ąíL‚Äčt|\mu\_{t}|\leq\hat{c}e^{-Lt}, and |ŌÉ1,t|‚Č§c^‚Äče‚ąíL‚Äčt|\sigma\_{1,t}|\leq\hat{c}e^{-Lt}, we get the desired estimate.
‚ąé

We first rewrite ([2.7](#S2.E7 "In 2 Candidate BSDE systems ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies")) in the form compatible with the framework of Section [3.2](#S3.SS2 "3.2 A general infinite-horizon BSDE system ‚Ä£ 3 A general system of infinite horizon BSDEs with stochastic Lipschitz drivers ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies"). Specifically, we consider the following formulation:

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
