## 4 The solvability of the control problem ([1.1](#S1.E1 "In 1 Introduction ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies"))-([1.2](#S1.E2 "In 1 Introduction ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies"))

In this section, we return to the infinite-horizon stochastic control problem ([1.1](#S1.E1 "In 1 Introduction ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies"))‚Äď([1.2](#S1.E2 "In 1 Introduction ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies")). Our goal is to address the solvability of the control problem in two parts.

First, leveraging the BSDE results developed in Section¬†[2](#S2 "2 Candidate BSDE systems ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies"), we prove that the value function of the control problem is finite and thus well-posed (see Definition¬†[4.1](#S4.Thmtheorem1 "Definition 4.1. ‚Ä£ 4.1 Wellposedness of the control problem ‚Ä£ 4 The solvability of the control problem (1.1)-(1.2) ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies")). To this end, we begin with the corresponding finite-horizon stochastic control problem and reformulate the cost functional as the sum of a fixed cost and a completed square term. We then pass to the infinite-horizon limit.

Second, under an additional assumption on the BSDE solution, we show that the fixed cost coincides with the value function of the control problem and derive the corresponding optimal strategy.

### 4.1 Wellposedness of the control problem

In this section, we prove that the control problem is wellposed in the following sense (refer to [[29](#bib.bib29)]):

###### Definition 4.1.

We say that the control problem ([1.1](#S1.E1 "In 1 Introduction ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies"))-([1.2](#S1.E2 "In 1 Introduction ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies")) is wellposed if

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | Vt‚Äč(ūĚí≥t‚ąí,i):=infX~‚ąąūĚíúJ‚Äč(t,ūĚí≥t‚ąí,i;X~)>‚ąí‚ąě.V\_{t}(\mathcal{X}\_{t-},i):=\inf\_{\widetilde{X}\in\mathscr{A}}J(t,\mathcal{X}\_{t-},i;\widetilde{X})>-\infty. |  | (4.1) |

From the expression ([1.1](#S1.E1 "In 1 Introduction ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies")), it is not immediately clear whether ([4.1](#S4.E1 "In Definition 4.1. ‚Ä£ 4.1 Wellposedness of the control problem ‚Ä£ 4 The solvability of the control problem (1.1)-(1.2) ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies")) holds. To verify ([4.1](#S4.E1 "In Definition 4.1. ‚Ä£ 4.1 Wellposedness of the control problem ‚Ä£ 4 The solvability of the control problem (1.1)-(1.2) ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies")), we first reformulate the cost functional ([1.1](#S1.E1 "In 1 Introduction ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies")) by considering its finite-horizon counterpart and then letting the horizon tend to infinity.

###### Lemma 4.2.

For any X~‚ąąūĚíú\widetilde{X}\in\mathscr{A}, define

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  | JT‚Äč(t,ūĚí≥t‚ąí,i;X~T)=ūĚĒľt‚Äč[‚ąętT(‚ąíY~s‚ąíT‚Äčd‚ÄčX~sT+ő≥s2‚Äčd‚Äč[X~T]s‚ąíŌÉ~sőĪs‚Äčd‚Äč[X~T,W]s)+‚ąętT(őĽsőĪs‚Äč(X~sT)2‚ąíŌē2‚ÄčY~sT‚ÄčX~sT)‚ÄčūĚĎĎs],J^{T}(t,\mathcal{X}\_{t-},i;\widetilde{X}^{T})=\mathbb{E}\_{t}\left[\int\_{t}^{T}\left(-\widetilde{Y}^{T}\_{s-}\,d\widetilde{X}^{T}\_{s}+\frac{\gamma\_{s}}{2}d[\widetilde{X}^{T}]\_{s}-\widetilde{\sigma}^{\alpha\_{s}}\_{s}\,d[\widetilde{X}^{T},W]\_{s}\right)+\int\_{t}^{T}\left(\lambda^{\alpha\_{s}}\_{s}(\widetilde{X}^{T}\_{s})^{2}-\frac{\phi}{2}\widetilde{Y}^{T}\_{s}\widetilde{X}^{T}\_{s}\right)\,ds\right], |  |

where X~sT=X~s‚ÄčūĚüŹ[t,T)‚Äč(s)\widetilde{X}^{T}\_{s}=\widetilde{X}\_{s}\mathbf{1}\_{[t,T)}(s)888This is essentially a liquidation strategy. For a non-liquidation alternative, additional terms of the form ‚ąí(Y~T‚ąí+ő≥T2‚ÄčX~T‚ąí)‚ÄčX~T‚ąíő≥T2‚ÄčX~T‚Äč(X~T‚ąíX~T‚ąí)-(\widetilde{Y}\_{T-}+\frac{\gamma\_{T}}{2}\widetilde{X}\_{T-})\widetilde{X}\_{T}-\frac{\gamma\_{T}}{2}\widetilde{X}\_{T}(\widetilde{X}\_{T}-\widetilde{X}\_{T-}) in the finite-horizon cost needs to be introduced and can be shown to vanish due to the integrability ([1.4](#S1.E4 "In item (ii) ‚Ä£ 1.1 Notation, convention, assumption and admissible space ‚Ä£ 1 Introduction ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies")) and ([1.5](#S1.E5 "In item (ii) ‚Ä£ 1.1 Notation, convention, assumption and admissible space ‚Ä£ 1 Introduction ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies")). The remainder of the analysis will follow a similar approach. and Y~T\widetilde{Y}^{T} is the corresponding state.
The cost with the finite-horizon and truncated strategy X~T\widetilde{X}^{T}, JT‚Äč(t,ūĚí≥t‚ąí,i;X~T)J^{T}(t,\mathcal{X}\_{t-},i;\widetilde{X}^{T}), can be reformulated as

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | JT‚Äč(t,ūĚí≥t‚ąí,i;X~T)=ūĚĒľt‚Äč[‚ąętT1asőĪs‚Äč(IsA¬Į,őĪs‚ÄčūĚí≥s+IsB¬Į,őĪs)2‚ÄčūĚĎĎs]+ūĚí≥t‚ąí‚ä§‚ÄčAti‚ÄčūĚí≥t‚ąí+ūĚí≥t‚ąí‚ä§‚ÄčBti+Cti+ūĚĒľt‚Äč[(12‚ąíA¬ĮTőĪT‚ąí)‚Äčő≥T‚ÄčP~T2‚ąíB¬ĮTőĪT‚ąí‚ÄčP~T‚ąíCTőĪT‚ąí],\begin{split}J^{T}(t,\mathcal{X}\_{t-},i;\widetilde{X}^{T})=&~\mathbb{E}\_{t}\left[\int\_{t}^{T}\frac{1}{a\_{s}^{\alpha\_{s}}}(I\_{s}^{\bar{A},\alpha\_{s}}\mathcal{X}\_{s}+I^{\bar{B},\alpha\_{s}}\_{s})^{2}\,ds\right]+\mathcal{X}^{\top}\_{t-}A^{i}\_{t}\mathcal{X}\_{t-}+\mathcal{X}^{\top}\_{t-}B^{i}\_{t}+C^{i}\_{t}\\ &+\mathbb{E}\_{t}\left[\left(\frac{1}{2}-\bar{A}^{\alpha\_{T-}}\_{T}\right)\gamma\_{T}\widetilde{P}^{2}\_{T}-\bar{B}^{\alpha\_{T-}}\_{T}\widetilde{P}\_{T}-C^{\alpha\_{T-}}\_{T}\right],\end{split} |  | (4.2) |

where the processes IA¬ĮI^{\bar{A}} and IB¬ĮI^{\bar{B}} are given by

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |

###### Proof.

For any admissible strategy X~\widetilde{X}, noting that (X~T,Y~T)=(X~,Y~)(\widetilde{X}^{T},\widetilde{Y}^{T})=(\widetilde{X},\widetilde{Y}) on [0,T)[0,T), we split the cost arising from the last jump from the cost:

###### Theorem 4.3.

For any X~‚ąąūĚíú\widetilde{X}\in\mathscr{A}, the cost functional for the control problem ([1.1](#S1.E1 "In 1 Introduction ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies"))-([1.2](#S1.E2 "In 1 Introduction ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies")) starting from (t,ūĚí≥t‚ąí,i)(t,\mathcal{X}\_{t-},i) can be rewritten as

| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | J‚Äč(t,ūĚí≥t‚ąí,i;X~)=ūĚĒľt‚Äč[‚ąęt‚ąě1asőĪs‚Äč(IsA,őĪs‚ÄčūĚí≥s+IsB,őĪs)2‚ÄčūĚĎĎs]+ūĚí≥t‚ąí‚ä§‚ÄčAti‚ÄčūĚí≥t‚ąí+ūĚí≥t‚ąí‚ä§‚ÄčBti+Cti,\begin{split}J(t,\mathcal{X}\_{t-},i;\widetilde{X})=&~\mathbb{E}\_{t}\left[\int\_{t}^{\infty}\frac{1}{a^{\alpha\_{s}}\_{s}}\left(I^{A,\alpha\_{s}}\_{s}\mathcal{X}\_{s}+I^{B,\alpha\_{s}}\_{s}\right)^{2}\,ds\right]+\mathcal{X}^{\top}\_{t-}A\_{t}^{i}\mathcal{X}\_{t-}+\mathcal{X}^{\top}\_{t-}B\_{t}^{i}+C\_{t}^{i},\end{split} |  | (4.8) |

where we recall ūĚí≥=(X~,Y~)‚ä§{\cal X}=(\widetilde{X},\widetilde{Y})^{\top}.

In particular, infX~‚ąąūĚíúJ‚Äč(t,ūĚí≥t‚ąí,i;X~)>‚ąí‚ąě\inf\_{\widetilde{X}\in\mathscr{A}}J(t,\mathcal{X}\_{t-},i;\widetilde{X})>-\infty, and infinite-horizon control problem ([1.1](#S1.E1 "In 1 Introduction ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies"))-([1.2](#S1.E2 "In 1 Introduction ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies")) is wellposed in the sesne of Definition [4.1](#S4.Thmtheorem1 "Definition 4.1. ‚Ä£ 4.1 Wellposedness of the control problem ‚Ä£ 4 The solvability of the control problem (1.1)-(1.2) ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies"). Moreover, the optimal strategy is unique whenever it exists.

###### Proof.

First, by monotone convergence theorem we have the convergence of the first term in ([4.2](#S4.E2 "In Lemma 4.2. ‚Ä£ 4.1 Wellposedness of the control problem ‚Ä£ 4 The solvability of the control problem (1.1)-(1.2) ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies"))

| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | limT‚Üí‚ąěūĚĒľt‚Äč[‚ąętT1asőĪs‚Äč(IsA,őĪs‚ÄčūĚí≥s+IsB,őĪs)2‚ÄčūĚĎĎs]=ūĚĒľt‚Äč[‚ąęt‚ąě1asőĪs‚Äč(IsA,őĪs‚ÄčūĚí≥s+IsB,őĪs)2‚ÄčūĚĎĎs].\displaystyle\lim\_{T\rightarrow\infty}\mathbb{E}\_{t}\left[\int\_{t}^{T}\frac{1}{a^{\alpha\_{s}}\_{s}}\left(I\_{s}^{A,\alpha\_{s}}\mathcal{X}\_{s}+I^{B,\alpha\_{s}}\_{s}\right)^{2}\,ds\right]=\mathbb{E}\_{t}\left[\int\_{t}^{\infty}\frac{1}{a^{\alpha\_{s}}\_{s}}\left(I\_{s}^{A,\alpha\_{s}}\mathcal{X}\_{s}+I^{B,\alpha\_{s}}\_{s}\right)^{2}\,ds\right]. |  | (4.9) |

Second, due to ([1.5](#S1.E5 "In item (ii) ‚Ä£ 1.1 Notation, convention, assumption and admissible space ‚Ä£ 1 Introduction ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies")), Proposition¬†[A.1](#A1.Thmtheorem1 "Proposition A.1. ‚Ä£ Appendix A Results on ūĚźī. ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies"), Lemma¬†[3.8](#S3.Thmtheorem8 "Lemma 3.8. ‚Ä£ 3.3 The BSDE Systems (2.4)-(2.9): Existence ‚Ä£ 3 A general system of infinite horizon BSDEs with stochastic Lipschitz drivers ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies"), Theorem¬†[3.10](#S3.Thmtheorem10 "Theorem 3.10. ‚Ä£ 3.3 The BSDE Systems (2.4)-(2.9): Existence ‚Ä£ 3 A general system of infinite horizon BSDEs with stochastic Lipschitz drivers ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies") and Theorem [3.11](#S3.Thmtheorem11 "Theorem 3.11. ‚Ä£ 3.3 The BSDE Systems (2.4)-(2.9): Existence ‚Ä£ 3 A general system of infinite horizon BSDEs with stochastic Lipschitz drivers ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies"), we obtain the following convergence

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | |ūĚĒľt‚Äč[(12‚ąíA¬ĮTőĪT‚ąí)‚Äčő≥T‚ÄčP~T2‚ąíB¬ĮTőĪT‚ąí‚ÄčP~T‚ąíCTőĪT‚ąí]|‚Č§c‚Äče‚ąí2‚ÄčŌÜ‚ÄčT‚ÄčūĚĒľt‚Äč[sups‚Č•te2‚ÄčŌÜ‚Äčs‚Äčő≥s‚ÄčP~s2]+c‚Äče‚ąíő≤4‚ÄčT‚Äč‚ÄĖB¬Į‚ÄĖ‚ąě,‚ąíő≤4‚ÄčūĚĒľt‚Äč[sups‚Č•te2‚ÄčŌÜ‚Äčs‚Äčő≥s‚ÄčP~s2]1/2‚ÄčūĚĒľt‚Äč[sups‚Č•t1ő≥s]1/2+c‚Äče‚ąíő≤‚ÄčT8‚ÄčūĚĒľt‚Äč[sups‚Č•teő≤‚Äčs4‚Äč|Cs|2]1/2‚Üí0,as¬†‚ÄčT‚Üí‚ąě.\begin{split}&~\left|\mathbb{E}\_{t}\left[\left(\frac{1}{2}-\bar{A}\_{T}^{\alpha\_{T-}}\right)\gamma\_{T}\widetilde{P}^{2}\_{T}-\bar{B}\_{T}^{\alpha\_{T-}}\widetilde{P}\_{T}-C^{\alpha\_{T-}}\_{T}\right]\right|\\ \leq&~ce^{-2\varphi T}\mathbb{E}\_{t}\left[\sup\_{s\geq t}e^{2\varphi s}\gamma\_{s}\widetilde{P}^{2}\_{s}\right]+ce^{-\frac{\beta}{4}T}\|\bar{B}\|\_{\infty,-\frac{\beta}{4}}\mathbb{E}\_{t}\left[\sup\_{s\geq t}e^{2\varphi s}\gamma\_{s}\widetilde{P}^{2}\_{s}\right]^{1/2}\mathbb{E}\_{t}\left[\sup\_{s\geq t}\frac{1}{\gamma\_{s}}\right]^{1/2}\\ &~+ce^{-\frac{\beta T}{8}}\mathbb{E}\_{t}\left[\sup\_{s\geq t}e^{\frac{\beta s}{4}}\left|C\_{s}\right|^{2}\right]^{1/2}\\ \rightarrow&~0,\qquad\text{as }T\rightarrow\infty.\end{split} |  | (4.10) |

Therefore, the right hand side of ([4.2](#S4.E2 "In Lemma 4.2. ‚Ä£ 4.1 Wellposedness of the control problem ‚Ä£ 4 The solvability of the control problem (1.1)-(1.2) ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies")) converges to the right hand side of ([4.8](#S4.E8 "In Theorem 4.3. ‚Ä£ 4.1 Wellposedness of the control problem ‚Ä£ 4 The solvability of the control problem (1.1)-(1.2) ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies")). It remains to verify the convergence of the left hand side.

To do so, note the following convergence

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | |ūĚĒľt‚Äč[12‚Äčő≥T‚ÄčX~T‚ąí2+X~T‚ąí‚ÄčY~T‚ąí]|=|ūĚĒľt‚Äč[‚ąí12‚Äčő≥T‚ÄčX~T‚ąí2+ő≥T‚ÄčX~T‚ąí‚ÄčP~T]|‚Č§c‚Äče‚ąí2‚ÄčŌÜ‚ÄčT‚ÄčūĚĒľt‚Äč[sups‚Č•te2‚ÄčŌÜ‚Äčs‚Äčő≥s‚ÄčX~s2]+c‚Äče‚ąí2‚ÄčŌÜ‚ÄčT‚ÄčūĚĒľt‚Äč[sups‚Č•te2‚ÄčŌÜ‚Äčs‚Äčő≥s‚ÄčX~s2]1/2‚ÄčūĚĒľt‚Äč[sups‚Č•te2‚ÄčŌÜ‚Äčs‚Äčő≥s‚ÄčP~s2]1/2‚Üí0,as¬†‚ÄčT‚Üí‚ąě.\begin{split}&~\left|\mathbb{E}\_{t}\left[\frac{1}{2}\gamma\_{T}\widetilde{X}^{2}\_{T-}+\widetilde{X}\_{T-}\widetilde{Y}\_{T-}\right]\right|=\left|\mathbb{E}\_{t}\left[-\frac{1}{2}\gamma\_{T}\widetilde{X}^{2}\_{T-}+\gamma\_{T}\widetilde{X}\_{T-}\widetilde{P}\_{T}\right]\right|\\ \leq&~ce^{-2\varphi T}\mathbb{E}\_{t}\left[\sup\_{s\geq t}e^{2\varphi s}\gamma\_{s}\widetilde{X}^{2}\_{s}\right]+ce^{-2\varphi T}\mathbb{E}\_{t}\left[\sup\_{s\geq t}e^{2\varphi s}\gamma\_{s}\widetilde{X}^{2}\_{s}\right]^{1/2}\mathbb{E}\_{t}\left[\sup\_{s\geq t}e^{2\varphi s}\gamma\_{s}\widetilde{P}^{2}\_{s}\right]^{1/2}\\ \rightarrow&~0,\qquad\text{as }T\rightarrow\infty.\end{split} |  | (4.11) |

From the integrability ([1.4](#S1.E4 "In item (ii) ‚Ä£ 1.1 Notation, convention, assumption and admissible space ‚Ä£ 1 Introduction ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies")) and ([1.5](#S1.E5 "In item (ii) ‚Ä£ 1.1 Notation, convention, assumption and admissible space ‚Ä£ 1 Introduction ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies")), the supremum over T‚Č•0T\geq 0 of all the stochastic integrals in ([4.7](#S4.E7 "In Proof. ‚Ä£ 4.1 Wellposedness of the control problem ‚Ä£ 4 The solvability of the control problem (1.1)-(1.2) ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies")) is integrable. By the dominated convergence theorem and ([4.11](#S4.E11 "In Proof. ‚Ä£ 4.1 Wellposedness of the control problem ‚Ä£ 4 The solvability of the control problem (1.1)-(1.2) ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies")), we get the convergence of the left hand side and thus the equality ([4.8](#S4.E8 "In Theorem 4.3. ‚Ä£ 4.1 Wellposedness of the control problem ‚Ä£ 4 The solvability of the control problem (1.1)-(1.2) ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies")).
‚ąé

### 4.2 Existence of an optimal strategy

We construct the candidate optimal strategy in the following order:

‚ąô\bullet Define the ‚Ąď\ell-dimentional processes ŌÄ=(ŌÄs)s‚Č•0\pi=(\pi\_{s})\_{s\geq 0} in terms of (A¬Į,ZA¬Į)(\bar{A},Z^{\bar{A}}) by

|  |  |  |

|  | ŌÄi=ő≥ai‚Äč(őĽiő≥+(ŌĀi+őľ)‚ÄčA¬Įi+ŌÉ1‚ÄčZA¬Į,i),i‚ąą‚Ą≥.\pi^{i}=\frac{\gamma}{a^{i}}\left(\frac{\lambda^{i}}{\gamma}+(\rho^{i}+\mu)\bar{A}^{i}+\sigma\_{1}Z^{\bar{A},i}\right),\quad i\in\cal M. |  |

###### Assumption 4.4.

For some 0<KŌÄ<L0<K\_{\pi}<L, |ŌÄ|2‚ąąHBMO2,KŌÄ‚Äč‚čāS2,0|\pi|^{2}\in H^{2,K\_{\pi}}\_{\text{BMO}}\bigcap S^{2,0} and ő∑‚ąąS4,‚ąíŌÜ\eta\in S^{4,-\varphi}.

###### Remark 4.5.

Assumption¬†[4.4](#S4.Thmtheorem4 "Assumption 4.4. ‚Ä£ 4.2 Existence of an optimal strategy ‚Ä£ 4 The solvability of the control problem (1.1)-(1.2) ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies") seems strong, but it plays a crucial role in verifying that X~‚ąó‚ąąūĚíú\widetilde{X}^{\*}\in\mathscr{A}. Essentially, it requires that |ŌÉ1‚ÄčZA¬Į|2‚ąąHBMO2,KŌÄ‚Äč‚čāS2,0|\sigma\_{1}Z^{\bar{A}}|^{2}\in H^{2,K\_{\pi}}\_{\text{BMO}}\bigcap S^{2,0} and that supt|ŌÉ1,t‚ÄčZtB¬Į|\sup\_{t}|\sigma\_{1,t}Z^{\bar{B}}\_{t}| is integrable to the fourth power. A similar assumption is also made in [[1](#bib.bib1), Theorem 3.4 and Remark 3.5(b)]. These conditions are trivially satisfied when ŌÉ1=0\sigma\_{1}=0 or (ZA¬Į,ZB¬Į)(Z^{\bar{A}},Z^{\bar{B}}) are bounded.

###### Theorem 4.6.

Let Assumption [1.1](#S1.Thmtheorem1 "Assumption 1.1. ‚Ä£ 1.1 Notation, convention, assumption and admissible space ‚Ä£ 1 Introduction ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies") and Assumption [4.4](#S4.Thmtheorem4 "Assumption 4.4. ‚Ä£ 4.2 Existence of an optimal strategy ‚Ä£ 4 The solvability of the control problem (1.1)-(1.2) ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies") hold.

* i)

  The value function defined in Definition [4.1](#S4.Thmtheorem1 "Definition 4.1. ‚Ä£ 4.1 Wellposedness of the control problem ‚Ä£ 4 The solvability of the control problem (1.1)-(1.2) ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies"), starting at 0 for the infinite-horizon control problem ([1.1](#S1.E1 "In 1 Introduction ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies"))-([1.2](#S1.E2 "In 1 Introduction ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies")), satisfies

  |  |  |  |  |
  | --- | --- | --- | --- |
  |  | V0‚Äč(ūĚí≥0‚ąí,i0)=ūĚí≥0‚ąí‚ä§‚ÄčA0i0‚ÄčūĚí≥0‚ąí+ūĚí≥0‚ąí‚ä§‚ÄčB0i0+C0i0.V\_{0}(\mathcal{X}\_{0-},i\_{0})=\mathcal{X}^{\top}\_{0-}A^{i\_{0}}\_{0}\mathcal{X}\_{0-}+\mathcal{X}^{\top}\_{0-}B^{i\_{0}}\_{0}+C^{i\_{0}}\_{0}. |  | (4.15) |
* ii)

  If X~‚ąó\widetilde{X}^{\*} defined by ([4.13](#S4.E13 "In 4.2 Existence of an optimal strategy ‚Ä£ 4 The solvability of the control problem (1.1)-(1.2) ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies"))-([4.14](#S4.E14 "In 4.2 Existence of an optimal strategy ‚Ä£ 4 The solvability of the control problem (1.1)-(1.2) ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies")) is a c√†dl√†g semimartingale, then the pair (Xt‚ąó,Yt‚ąó):=(eŌē2‚Äčt‚ÄčX~t‚ąó,eŌē2‚Äčt‚ÄčY~t‚ąó)(X^{\*}\_{t},Y^{\*}\_{t}):=(e^{\frac{\phi}{2}t}\widetilde{X}^{\*}\_{t},e^{\frac{\phi}{2}t}\widetilde{Y}^{\*}\_{t}) is the unique optimal control-state pair for the infinite-horizon control problem ([1.1](#S1.E1 "In 1 Introduction ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies"))-([1.2](#S1.E2 "In 1 Introduction ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies")).

###### Remark 4.7.

If X~‚ąó\widetilde{X}^{\*} is not a semimartingale, then the value function ([4.15](#S4.E15 "In item i) ‚Ä£ Theorem 4.6. ‚Ä£ 4.2 Existence of an optimal strategy ‚Ä£ 4 The solvability of the control problem (1.1)-(1.2) ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies")) can only be approximated but cannot be reached by any admissible strategy in ūĚíú\mathscr{A}.

The following lemma plays a crucial role in establishing the admissible integrability of X~‚ąó\widetilde{X}^{\*} and P~‚ąó\widetilde{P}^{\*}.

###### Lemma 4.8.

Let ő∂\zeta and őł\theta be two processes such that ő∂‚ąąHBMO2,Kő∂\zeta\in H^{2,K\_{\zeta}}\_{\text{BMO}} and őł2‚ąąHBMO2,Kőł\theta^{2}\in H^{2,K\_{\theta}}\_{\text{BMO}} with Kőł<0K\_{\theta}<0. For any K>Kő∂K>K\_{\zeta} and t‚Č•0t\geq 0 denote

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  | őďt:=exp‚Ā°{‚ąę0te‚ąíK‚Äčs‚Äčő∂s‚ÄčūĚĎĎs+‚ąę0tőłs‚ÄčūĚĎĎWs}.\Gamma\_{t}:=\exp\left\{\int^{t}\_{0}e^{-Ks}\zeta\_{s}\,ds+\int^{t}\_{0}\theta\_{s}\,dW\_{s}\right\}. |  |

We have for any p‚Č•1p\geq 1

|  |  |  |

###### Proof.

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  | ūĚĒľ‚Äč[supt‚Č•0|őďt|p]‚Č§ūĚĒľ‚Äč[supt‚Č•0exp‚Ā°{2‚Äčp‚Äč‚ąę0te‚ąíK‚Äčs‚Äčő∂s‚ÄčūĚĎĎs+p2‚Äč‚ąę0tőłs2‚ÄčūĚĎĎs}]1/2‚ÄčūĚĒľ‚Äč[supt‚Č•0Lt2]1/2,\displaystyle\mathbb{E}\left[\sup\_{t\geq 0}|\Gamma\_{t}|^{p}\right]\leq\mathbb{E}\left[\sup\_{t\geq 0}\exp\left\{2p\int^{t}\_{0}e^{-Ks}\zeta\_{s}\,\,ds+p^{2}\int^{t}\_{0}\theta\_{s}^{2}\,ds\right\}\right]^{1/2}\mathbb{E}\left[\sup\_{t\geq 0}L\_{t}^{2}\right]^{1/2}, |  |

where

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  | Lt:=exp‚Ā°{‚ąí‚ąę0t(p‚Äčőłs)22‚ÄčūĚĎĎs+‚ąę0tp‚Äčőłs‚ÄčūĚĎĎWs}.L\_{t}:=\exp\left\{-\int^{t}\_{0}\frac{(p\theta\_{s})^{2}}{2}\,ds+\int^{t}\_{0}p\theta\_{s}\,dW\_{s}\right\}. |  |

Next, we prove the above two expectations are finite.

First, since ő∂‚ąąHBMO2,Kő∂\zeta\in H^{2,K\_{\zeta}}\_{\text{BMO}} and őł2‚ąąHBMO2,Kőł\theta^{2}\in H^{2,K\_{\theta}}\_{\text{BMO}}, by H√∂lder‚Äôs inequality and applying Lemma [3.1](#S3.Thmtheorem1 "Lemma 3.1. ‚Ä£ 3.1 Preliminary lemmas ‚Ä£ 3 A general system of infinite horizon BSDEs with stochastic Lipschitz drivers ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies") to ő∂\zeta and őł2\theta^{2}, we obtain

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  |  | ūĚĒľ‚Äč[supt‚Č•0exp‚Ā°{2‚Äčp‚Äč‚ąę0te‚ąíK‚Äčs‚Äčő∂s‚ÄčūĚĎĎs+p2‚Äč‚ąę0tőłs2‚ÄčūĚĎĎs}]\displaystyle~\mathbb{E}\left[\sup\_{t\geq 0}\exp\left\{2p\int^{t}\_{0}e^{-Ks}\zeta\_{s}\,ds+p^{2}\int^{t}\_{0}\theta\_{s}^{2}\,ds\right\}\right] |  |

| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | ‚Č§\displaystyle\leq | ūĚĒľ‚Äč[exp‚Ā°{4‚Äčp‚Äč‚ąę0‚ąěe‚ąíK‚Äčs‚Äč|ő∂s|‚ÄčūĚĎĎs}]1/2‚ÄčūĚĒľ‚Äč[exp‚Ā°{2‚Äčp2‚Äč‚ąę0‚ąěőłs2‚ÄčūĚĎĎs}]1/2\displaystyle~\mathbb{E}\left[\exp\left\{4p\int^{\infty}\_{0}e^{-Ks}|\zeta\_{s}|\,ds\right\}\right]^{1/2}\mathbb{E}\left[\exp\left\{2p^{2}\int^{\infty}\_{0}\theta\_{s}^{2}\,ds\right\}\right]^{1/2} |  |
|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | <\displaystyle< | ‚ąě.\displaystyle~\infty. |  |

Second, by Novikov‚Äôs criterion and Lemma [3.1](#S3.Thmtheorem1 "Lemma 3.1. ‚Ä£ 3.1 Preliminary lemmas ‚Ä£ 3 A general system of infinite horizon BSDEs with stochastic Lipschitz drivers ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies"), LsL\_{s} is a true martingale. It follows from Doob‚Äôs maximal inequality and H√∂lder‚Äôs inequality that

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  |  | ūĚĒľ‚Äč[supt‚Č•0(exp‚Ā°{‚ąí‚ąę0t(p‚Äčőłs)22‚ÄčūĚĎĎs+‚ąę0tp‚Äčőłs‚ÄčūĚĎĎWs})2]\displaystyle~\mathbb{E}\left[\sup\_{t\geq 0}\left(\exp\left\{-\int^{t}\_{0}\frac{(p\theta\_{s})^{2}}{2}\,ds+\int^{t}\_{0}p\theta\_{s}\,dW\_{s}\right\}\right)^{2}\right] |  |
|  |  |  |  |

|  | ‚Č§\displaystyle\leq | 4‚ÄčūĚĒľ‚Äč[exp‚Ā°{‚ąí‚ąę0‚ąě(p‚Äčőłs)2‚ÄčūĚĎĎs+2‚Äč‚ąę0‚ąěp‚Äčőłs‚ÄčūĚĎĎWs}]\displaystyle~4\mathbb{E}\left[\exp\left\{-\int\_{0}^{\infty}(p\theta\_{s})^{2}\,ds+2\int\_{0}^{\infty}p\theta\_{s}\,dW\_{s}\right\}\right] |  |
|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | ‚Č§\displaystyle\leq | ūĚĒľ‚Äč[exp‚Ā°{4‚Äč‚ąę0‚ąěp‚Äčőłs‚ÄčūĚĎĎWs‚ąí8‚Äč‚ąę0‚ąě(p‚Äčőłs)2‚ÄčūĚĎĎs}]1/2‚ÄčūĚĒľ‚Äč[exp‚Ā°{6‚Äčp2‚Äč‚ąę0‚ąěőłs2‚ÄčūĚĎĎs}]1/2\displaystyle~\mathbb{E}\left[\exp\left\{4\int\_{0}^{\infty}p\theta\_{s}\,dW\_{s}-8\int\_{0}^{\infty}(p\theta\_{s})^{2}\,ds\right\}\right]^{1/2}\mathbb{E}\left[\exp\left\{6p^{2}\int\_{0}^{\infty}\theta^{2}\_{s}\,ds\right\}\right]^{1/2} |  |
|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | =\displaystyle= | ūĚĒľ‚Äč[exp‚Ā°{6‚Äčp2‚Äč‚ąę0‚ąěőłs2‚ÄčūĚĎĎs}]1/2\displaystyle~\mathbb{E}\left[\exp\left\{6p^{2}\int\_{0}^{\infty}\theta^{2}\_{s}\,ds\right\}\right]^{1/2} |  |
|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | <\displaystyle< | ‚ąě,\displaystyle~\infty, |  |

where the last step is given by Lemma [3.1](#S3.Thmtheorem1 "Lemma 3.1. ‚Ä£ 3.1 Preliminary lemmas ‚Ä£ 3 A general system of infinite horizon BSDEs with stochastic Lipschitz drivers ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies").
‚ąé

Using Lemma¬†[4.8](#S4.Thmtheorem8 "Lemma 4.8. ‚Ä£ 4.2 Existence of an optimal strategy ‚Ä£ 4 The solvability of the control problem (1.1)-(1.2) ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies"), we can establish the integrability result stated in the next lemma.

###### Lemma 4.9.

Let Assumption [1.1](#S1.Thmtheorem1 "Assumption 1.1. ‚Ä£ 1.1 Notation, convention, assumption and admissible space ‚Ä£ 1 Introduction ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies") and Assumption [4.4](#S4.Thmtheorem4 "Assumption 4.4. ‚Ä£ 4.2 Existence of an optimal strategy ‚Ä£ 4 The solvability of the control problem (1.1)-(1.2) ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies") hold.
The processes P~‚ąó\widetilde{P}^{\*} and X~‚ąó\widetilde{X}^{\*} defined in ([4.12](#S4.E12 "In 4.2 Existence of an optimal strategy ‚Ä£ 4 The solvability of the control problem (1.1)-(1.2) ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies")) and ([4.13](#S4.E13 "In 4.2 Existence of an optimal strategy ‚Ä£ 4 The solvability of the control problem (1.1)-(1.2) ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies")) satisfy the integrability ([1.4](#S1.E4 "In item (ii) ‚Ä£ 1.1 Notation, convention, assumption and admissible space ‚Ä£ 1 Introduction ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies")) and ([1.5](#S1.E5 "In item (ii) ‚Ä£ 1.1 Notation, convention, assumption and admissible space ‚Ä£ 1 Introduction ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies")).

###### Proof.

We begin by deriving an estimate of ő≥s‚ÄčP~‚ąó\gamma\_{s}\widetilde{P}^{\*}, which satisfies the SDE:

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  | {d‚Äč(ő≥s‚ÄčP~s‚ąó)=(q¬ĮsőĪs‚Äčő≥s‚ÄčP~s‚ąó‚ąí(ŌĀsőĪs+őľs)‚Äčő≥s‚Äčő∑sőĪs)‚Äčd‚Äčs+(ŌÉ1,s‚Äč(1‚ąíŌÄsőĪs)‚Äčő≥s‚ÄčP~s‚ąó‚ąíŌÉ1,s‚Äčő≥s‚Äčő∑sőĪs+ŌÉ~sőĪs)‚Äčd‚ÄčWs,ő≥0‚ÄčP~0‚ąó=ő≥0‚Äčx0,\left\{\begin{aligned} d(\gamma\_{s}\widetilde{P}^{\*}\_{s})=&~\left(\bar{q}^{\alpha\_{s}}\_{s}\gamma\_{s}\widetilde{P}^{\*}\_{s}-(\rho^{\alpha\_{s}}\_{s}+\mu\_{s})\gamma\_{s}\eta^{\alpha\_{s}}\_{s}\right)\,ds+\Big(\sigma\_{1,s}(1-\pi^{\alpha\_{s}}\_{s})\gamma\_{s}\widetilde{P}^{\*}\_{s}-\sigma\_{1,s}\gamma\_{s}\eta^{\alpha\_{s}}\_{s}+\widetilde{\sigma}\_{s}^{\alpha\_{s}}\Big)\,dW\_{s},\\ \gamma\_{0}\widetilde{P}^{\*}\_{0}=&~\gamma\_{0}x\_{0},\end{aligned}\right. |  |

where

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  | q¬ĮsőĪs:=őľs‚ąí(Ōē2+(ŌĀsőĪs+őľs)‚ÄčŌÄsőĪs)=őľs‚ąí(ŌĀsőĪs+őľs)‚Äčő≥s‚ÄčŌÉ1,s‚ÄčZsA¬Į,őĪsasőĪs‚ąíŌē2‚ąíőĽsőĪs‚Äč(ŌĀsőĪs+őľs)+ő≥s‚Äč(ŌĀsőĪs+őľs)2‚ÄčA¬ĮsőĪsasőĪs:=őľs‚ąí(ŌĀsőĪs+őľs)‚Äčő≥s‚ÄčŌÉ1,s‚ÄčZsA¬Į,őĪsasőĪs‚ąíq^sőĪs.\begin{split}\bar{q}^{\alpha\_{s}}\_{s}:=&~\mu\_{s}-\left(\frac{\phi}{2}+(\rho^{\alpha\_{s}}\_{s}+\mu\_{s})\pi\_{s}^{\alpha\_{s}}\right)\\ =&~\mu\_{s}-(\rho\_{s}^{\alpha\_{s}}+\mu\_{s})\frac{\gamma\_{s}\sigma\_{1,s}Z^{\bar{A},\alpha\_{s}}\_{s}}{a\_{s}^{\alpha\_{s}}}-\frac{\phi}{2}-\frac{\lambda\_{s}^{\alpha\_{s}}(\rho\_{s}^{\alpha\_{s}}+\mu\_{s})+\gamma\_{s}(\rho\_{s}^{\alpha\_{s}}+\mu\_{s})^{2}\bar{A}\_{s}^{\alpha\_{s}}}{a^{\alpha\_{s}}\_{s}}\\ :=&~\mu\_{s}-(\rho\_{s}^{\alpha\_{s}}+\mu\_{s})\frac{\gamma\_{s}\sigma\_{1,s}Z^{\bar{A},\alpha\_{s}}\_{s}}{a\_{s}^{\alpha\_{s}}}-\hat{q}^{\alpha\_{s}}\_{s}.\end{split} |  |

Note that the signs of the first two terms in q¬ĮőĪ\bar{q}^{\alpha} are indeterminate, and the coefficient of the linear term in the diffusion, that is, ŌÉ1‚Äč(1‚ąíŌÄőĪ)‚Äčő≥\sigma\_{1}(1-\pi^{\alpha})\gamma, is unbounded. To estimate ő≥‚ÄčP~‚ąó\gamma\widetilde{P}^{\*}, we first introduce two transformations that yield an SDE with a monotone driver and without unbounded linear term in the diffusion.

To eliminate the first two terms of q¬ĮőĪ\bar{q}^{\alpha} from the driver of ő≥‚ÄčP~‚ąó\gamma\widetilde{P}^{\*}, we consider the transformation őď‚Äčő≥‚ÄčP~‚ąó\Gamma\gamma\widetilde{P}^{\*}, where

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  | őď‚čÖ=exp‚Ā°{‚ąę0‚čÖ(‚ąíőľs+(ŌĀsőĪs+őľs)‚Äčő≥s‚ÄčŌÉ1,s‚ÄčZsA¬Į,őĪsasőĪs)‚ÄčūĚĎĎs}.\Gamma\_{\cdot}=\exp\left\{\int^{\cdot}\_{0}\left(-\mu\_{s}+\frac{(\rho^{\alpha\_{s}}\_{s}+\mu\_{s})\gamma\_{s}\sigma\_{1,s}Z\_{s}^{\bar{A},\alpha\_{s}}}{a^{\alpha\_{s}}\_{s}}\right)\,ds\right\}. |  |

It follows that

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  | d‚Äč(őďs‚Äčő≥s‚ÄčP~s‚ąó)=(‚ąíq^sőĪs‚Äčőďs‚Äčő≥s‚ÄčP~s‚ąó‚ąíőďs‚Äč(ŌĀsőĪs+őľs)‚Äčő≥s‚Äčő∑sőĪs)‚Äčd‚Äčs+(ŌÉ1,s‚Äč(1‚ąíŌÄsőĪs)‚Äčőďs‚Äčő≥s‚ÄčP~s‚ąó‚ąíőďs‚ÄčŌÉ1,s‚Äčő≥s‚Äčő∑sőĪs+őďs‚ÄčŌÉ~sőĪs)‚Äčd‚ÄčWs.d(\Gamma\_{s}\gamma\_{s}\widetilde{P}^{\*}\_{s})=\left(-\hat{q}^{\alpha\_{s}}\_{s}\Gamma\_{s}\gamma\_{s}\widetilde{P}^{\*}\_{s}-\Gamma\_{s}(\rho^{\alpha\_{s}}\_{s}+\mu\_{s})\gamma\_{s}\eta^{\alpha\_{s}}\_{s}\right)\,ds+\Big(\sigma\_{1,s}(1-\pi^{\alpha\_{s}}\_{s})\Gamma\_{s}\gamma\_{s}\widetilde{P}^{\*}\_{s}-\Gamma\_{s}\sigma\_{1,s}\gamma\_{s}\eta^{\alpha\_{s}}\_{s}+\Gamma\_{s}\widetilde{\sigma}\_{s}^{\alpha\_{s}}\Big)\,dW\_{s}. |  |

|  | d‚Äčőõs=‚ąíq^sőĪs‚Äčőõs‚Äčd‚Äčs‚ąíőďs‚Ąį^s‚Äč(ŌĀsőĪs+őľs)‚Äčő≥s‚Äčő∑sőĪs‚Äčd‚Äčs‚ąíőďs‚Ąį^s‚ÄčŌÉ1,s‚Äč(1‚ąíŌÄsőĪs)‚Äč(‚ąíŌÉ1,s‚Äčő≥s‚Äčő∑sőĪs+ŌÉ~sőĪs)‚Äčd‚Äčs‚ąíőďs‚Ąį^s‚Äč(ŌÉ1,s‚Äčő≥s‚Äčő∑sőĪs‚ąíŌÉ~sőĪs)‚Äčd‚ÄčWs.\begin{split}d\Lambda\_{s}=&~-\hat{q}^{\alpha\_{s}}\_{s}\Lambda\_{s}\,ds-\frac{\Gamma\_{s}}{\hat{\mathcal{E}}\_{s}}(\rho^{\alpha\_{s}}\_{s}+\mu\_{s})\gamma\_{s}\eta^{\alpha\_{s}}\_{s}\,ds-\frac{\Gamma\_{s}}{\hat{\mathcal{E}}\_{s}}\sigma\_{1,s}(1-\pi^{\alpha\_{s}}\_{s})(-\sigma\_{1,s}\gamma\_{s}\eta^{\alpha\_{s}}\_{s}+\widetilde{\sigma}\_{s}^{\alpha\_{s}})\,ds\\ &~-\frac{\Gamma\_{s}}{\hat{\mathcal{E}}\_{s}}(\sigma\_{1,s}\gamma\_{s}\eta^{\alpha\_{s}}\_{s}-\widetilde{\sigma}\_{s}^{\alpha\_{s}})\,dW\_{s}.\end{split} |  |

For őď‚Ąį^\frac{\Gamma}{\hat{\cal E}}, we have the following expression:

Recall 0<KŌÄ<L0<K\_{\pi}<L. Then for any constant KőłK\_{\theta} such that KŌÄ‚ąí2‚ÄčL<Kőł<0K\_{\pi}-2L<K\_{\theta}<0, it holds that by Assumption [4.4](#S4.Thmtheorem4 "Assumption 4.4. ‚Ä£ 4.2 Existence of an optimal strategy ‚Ä£ 4 The solvability of the control problem (1.1)-(1.2) ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies")

|  |  |  |

|  | ess‚ÄčsupŌĄ,ŌČ‚Ā°ūĚĒľŌĄ‚Äč[‚ąęŌĄ‚ąěe‚ąí2‚ÄčKőł‚Äčs‚Äč{ŌÉ1,s2‚Äč(1‚ąíŌÄs)2}2‚ÄčūĚĎĎs]‚Č§c‚Äčess‚ÄčsupŌĄ,ŌČ‚Ā°ūĚĒľŌĄ‚Äč[‚ąęŌĄ‚ąěe‚ąí2‚ÄčKőł‚Äčs‚ąí4‚ÄčL‚Äčs+2‚ÄčKŌÄ‚Äčs‚Äče‚ąí2‚ÄčKŌÄ‚Äčs‚Äč{(1‚ąíŌÄs)2}2‚ÄčūĚĎĎs]‚Č§c‚Äčess‚ÄčsupŌĄ,ŌČ‚Ā°ūĚĒľŌĄ‚Äč[‚ąęŌĄ‚ąěe‚ąí2‚ÄčKŌÄ‚Äčs‚Äč{(1‚ąíŌÄs)2}2‚ÄčūĚĎĎs]<‚ąě.\begin{split}\operatorname\*{ess\,sup}\_{\tau,\omega}\mathbb{E}\_{\tau}\left[\int\_{\tau}^{\infty}e^{-2K\_{\theta}s}\{\sigma\_{1,s}^{2}(1-\pi\_{s})^{2}\}^{2}\,ds\right]\leq&~c\operatorname\*{ess\,sup}\_{\tau,\omega}\mathbb{E}\_{\tau}\left[\int\_{\tau}^{\infty}e^{-2K\_{\theta}s-4Ls+2K\_{\pi}s}e^{-2K\_{\pi}s}\{(1-\pi\_{s})^{2}\}^{2}\,ds\right]\\ \leq&~c\operatorname\*{ess\,sup}\_{\tau,\omega}\mathbb{E}\_{\tau}\left[\int\_{\tau}^{\infty}e^{-2K\_{\pi}s}\{(1-\pi\_{s})^{2}\}^{2}\,ds\right]<\infty.\end{split} |  |

Moreover, by choosing 0<KA¬Į<L0<K\_{\bar{A}}<L we have

| --- | --- | --- |
|  | |‚ąíőľs+(ŌĀsőĪs+őľs)‚Äčő≥s‚ÄčŌÉ1,s‚ÄčZsA¬Į,őĪsasőĪs+12‚ÄčŌÉ1,s2‚Äč(1‚ąíŌÄs)2|‚Č§c‚Äče‚ąíL‚Äčs‚Äč{1+|ZsA¬Į,őĪs|+|ŌÄs|2},\left|-\mu\_{s}+\frac{(\rho^{\alpha\_{s}}\_{s}+\mu\_{s})\gamma\_{s}\sigma\_{1,s}Z^{\bar{A},\alpha\_{s}}\_{s}}{a^{\alpha\_{s}}\_{s}}+\frac{1}{2}\sigma\_{1,s}^{2}(1-\pi\_{s})^{2}\right|\leq ce^{-Ls}\left\{1+|Z^{\bar{A},\alpha\_{s}}\_{s}|+|\pi\_{s}|^{2}\right\}, |  |

where 1+ZA¬Į,őĪ+|ŌÄ|2‚ąąHBMO2,KA¬Į‚ą®KŌÄ1+Z^{\bar{A},\alpha}+|\pi|^{2}\in H^{2,K\_{\bar{A}}\vee K\_{\pi}}\_{\text{BMO}} and KŌÄ‚ą®KA¬Į<LK\_{\pi}\vee K\_{\bar{A}}<L. |  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | ūĚĒľ‚Äč[supt‚Č•0(őďt‚Ąį^t)p]<‚ąě.\begin{split}\mathbb{E}\left[\sup\_{t\geq 0}\left(\frac{\Gamma\_{t}}{\hat{\cal E}\_{t}}\right)^{p}\right]<\infty.\end{split} |  | (4.16) |

Similary, under the same requirement of KŌÄK\_{\pi} and KA¬ĮK\_{\bar{A}}, we also have

|  |  |  |  |

|  | ūĚĒľ‚Äč[supt‚Č•0(‚Ąį^tőďt)p]<‚ąě.\begin{split}\mathbb{E}\left[\sup\_{t\geq 0}\left(\frac{\hat{\cal E}\_{t}}{\Gamma\_{t}}\right)^{p}\right]<\infty.\end{split} |  | (4.17) |

Note that q^i\hat{q}^{i} satisfies the following estimate:

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  |  | ‚ąíq^i\displaystyle~-\hat{q}^{i} |  |
|  |  |  |  |

|  |  |  |  |

|  | ‚Č§\displaystyle\leq | ‚ąíŌē2‚ąíőĽsőĪs‚Äč(ŌĀsőĪs+őľs)őľs‚Äčő≥s2+ő≥s‚ÄčŌĀsőĪs+őĽsőĪs+Ōē‚Äčő≥s2(since¬†‚ÄčA¬Į‚Äč¬†is valued below¬†‚Äč1/2)\displaystyle~-\frac{\phi}{2}-\frac{\lambda\_{s}^{\alpha\_{s}}(\rho\_{s}^{\alpha\_{s}}+\mu\_{s})}{\frac{\mu\_{s}\gamma\_{s}}{2}+\gamma\_{s}\rho\_{s}^{\alpha\_{s}}+\lambda\_{s}^{\alpha\_{s}}+\frac{\phi\gamma\_{s}}{2}}\qquad(\text{since }\bar{A}\text{ is valued below }1/2) |  |
|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | =\displaystyle= | ‚ąíŌē2‚ąíőĽsőĪső≥s‚Äč(ŌĀsőĪs+őľs)őľs2+ŌĀsőĪs+őĽsőĪső≥s+Ōē2.\displaystyle~-\frac{\phi}{2}-\frac{\frac{\lambda\_{s}^{\alpha\_{s}}}{\gamma\_{s}}(\rho\_{s}^{\alpha\_{s}}+\mu\_{s})}{\frac{\mu\_{s}}{2}+\rho\_{s}^{\alpha\_{s}}+\frac{\lambda\_{s}^{\alpha\_{s}}}{\gamma\_{s}}+\frac{\phi}{2}}. |  |

Recalling that by Assumption [1.1](#S1.Thmtheorem1 "Assumption 1.1. ‚Ä£ 1.1 Notation, convention, assumption and admissible space ‚Ä£ 1 Introduction ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies") (iii) and the definition of ŌÜ\varphi, we have

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  | Ōē2+mini‚Ā°őĽsiő≥s‚Äč(ŌĀsi+őľs)őľs2+ŌĀsi+őĽsiő≥s+Ōē2‚ąíŌÜ>0¬†and¬†ő≤8‚ąíŌÜ>0,\frac{\phi}{2}+\min\_{i}\frac{\frac{\lambda\_{s}^{i}}{\gamma\_{s}}(\rho\_{s}^{i}+\mu\_{s})}{\frac{\mu\_{s}}{2}+\rho\_{s}^{i}+\frac{\lambda\_{s}^{i}}{\gamma\_{s}}+\frac{\phi}{2}}-\varphi>0\quad\text{ and }\quad\frac{\beta}{8}-\varphi>0, |  |

In particular, q^i‚ąíŌÜ>0\hat{q}^{i}-\varphi>0 for all i‚ąą‚Ą≥i\in\cal M.

By It√ī‚Äôs formula, it holds that

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  |  | e2‚ÄčŌÜ‚Äčt‚Äčőõt2+‚ąę0t2‚Äče2‚ÄčŌÜ‚Äčs‚Äčőõs2‚Äč(q^sőĪs‚ąíŌÜ)‚ÄčūĚĎĎs\displaystyle~e^{2\varphi t}\Lambda^{2}\_{t}+\int^{t}\_{0}2e^{2\varphi s}\Lambda\_{s}^{2}\left(\hat{q}^{\alpha\_{s}}\_{s}-\varphi\right)\,ds |  |
|  |  |  |  |

|  | =\displaystyle= | őõ02‚ąí‚ąę0t2‚Äče2‚ÄčŌÜ‚Äčs‚Äčőõs‚Äčőďs‚Ąį^s‚Äč{(ŌĀsőĪs+őľs)‚Äčő≥s‚Äčő∑sőĪs+ŌÉ1,s‚Äč(1‚ąíŌÄsőĪs)‚Äč(‚ąíŌÉ1,s‚Äčő≥s‚Äčő∑sőĪs+ŌÉ~sőĪs)}‚ÄčūĚĎĎs\displaystyle~\Lambda\_{0}^{2}-\int\_{0}^{t}2e^{2\varphi s}\Lambda\_{s}\frac{\Gamma\_{s}}{\hat{\mathcal{E}}\_{s}}\left\{(\rho^{\alpha\_{s}}\_{s}+\mu\_{s})\gamma\_{s}\eta\_{s}^{\alpha\_{s}}+\sigma\_{1,s}(1-\pi\_{s}^{\alpha\_{s}})(-\sigma\_{1,s}\gamma\_{s}\eta\_{s}^{\alpha\_{s}}+\widetilde{\sigma}^{\alpha\_{s}}\_{s})\right\}\,ds |  |
|  |  |  |  |

|  |  | +‚ąę0te2‚ÄčŌÜ‚Äčs‚Äč(őďs‚Ąį^s)2‚Äč(ŌÉ1,s‚Äčő≥s‚Äčő∑sőĪs‚ąíŌÉ~sőĪs)2‚ÄčūĚĎĎs\displaystyle~+\int\_{0}^{t}e^{2\varphi s}\left(\frac{\Gamma\_{s}}{\hat{\mathcal{E}}\_{s}}\right)^{2}\left(\sigma\_{1,s}\gamma\_{s}\eta\_{s}^{\alpha\_{s}}-\widetilde{\sigma}\_{s}^{\alpha\_{s}}\right)^{2}\,ds |  |
|  |  |  |  |

|  |  | ‚ąí‚ąę0t2‚Äče2‚ÄčŌÜ‚Äčs‚Äčőõs‚Äčőďs‚Ąį^s‚Äč(ŌÉ1,s‚Äčő≥s‚Äčő∑sőĪs‚ąíŌÉ~sőĪs)‚ÄčūĚĎĎWs.\displaystyle~-\int\_{0}^{t}2e^{2\varphi s}\Lambda\_{s}\frac{\Gamma\_{s}}{\hat{\mathcal{E}}\_{s}}(\sigma\_{1,s}\gamma\_{s}\eta\_{s}^{\alpha\_{s}}-\widetilde{\sigma}^{\alpha\_{s}}\_{s})\,dW\_{s}. |  |

Taking ūĚĒľ‚Äč[supt‚Č•0(‚Ä¶)p]\mathbb{E}\left[\sup\_{t\geq 0}(\dots)^{p}\right] for any p‚Č•1p\geq 1 on both sides, using q^i>ŌÜ\hat{q}^{i}>\varphi and BDG‚Äôs inequality in the first inequality, and using Young‚Äôs inequality in the second one, we have

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  |  | ūĚĒľ‚Äč[supt‚Č•0e2‚Äčp‚ÄčŌÜ‚Äčt‚Äč|őõt|2‚Äčp]\displaystyle~\mathbb{E}\left[\sup\_{t\geq 0}e^{2p\varphi t}|\Lambda\_{t}|^{2p}\right] |  |

###### Proof of Theorem [4.6](#S4.Thmtheorem6 "Theorem 4.6. ‚Ä£ 4.2 Existence of an optimal strategy ‚Ä£ 4 The solvability of the control problem (1.1)-(1.2) ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies").

Moreover, it is easy to check that IA¬Į,i‚ÄčūĚí≥‚ąó+IB¬Į,i=0I^{\bar{A},i}\mathcal{X}^{\*}+I^{\bar{B},i}=0 for ūĚí≥‚ąó:=(X~‚ąó,Y~‚ąó)‚ä§{\mathcal{X}^{\*}}:=(\widetilde{X}^{\*},\widetilde{Y}^{\*})^{\top} defined in ([4.13](#S4.E13 "In 4.2 Existence of an optimal strategy ‚Ä£ 4 The solvability of the control problem (1.1)-(1.2) ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies")), for any i‚ąą‚Ą≥i\in\cal M. Thus, X~‚ąó\widetilde{X}^{\*} in ([4.13](#S4.E13 "In 4.2 Existence of an optimal strategy ‚Ä£ 4 The solvability of the control problem (1.1)-(1.2) ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies")) and ([4.14](#S4.E14 "In 4.2 Existence of an optimal strategy ‚Ä£ 4 The solvability of the control problem (1.1)-(1.2) ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies")) is optimal if it is a c√†dl√†g semimartingale.

It remains to verify the initial jump ([4.14](#S4.E14 "In 4.2 Existence of an optimal strategy ‚Ä£ 4 The solvability of the control problem (1.1)-(1.2) ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies")) is optimal. Note that after the initial jump, it should hold I0A¬Į,i‚ÄčūĚí≥0+I0B¬Į,i=0I^{\bar{A},i}\_{0}\mathcal{X}\_{0}+I^{\bar{B},i}\_{0}=0, equivalently, we have

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  | I1,0A¬Į,i‚ÄčX~0+I2,0A¬Į,i‚ÄčY~0+I0B¬Į,i=I1,0A¬Į,i‚Äč(X0‚ąí+őĒ‚ÄčX0)+I2,0A¬Į,i‚Äč(Y0‚ąí+őĒ‚ÄčY0)+I0B¬Į,i=0,I^{\bar{A},i}\_{1,0}\widetilde{X}\_{0}+I^{\bar{A},i}\_{2,0}\widetilde{Y}\_{0}+I^{\bar{B},i}\_{0}=I^{\bar{A},i}\_{1,0}(X\_{0-}+\Delta X\_{0})+I^{\bar{A},i}\_{2,0}(Y\_{0-}+\Delta Y\_{0})+I^{\bar{B},i}\_{0}=0, |  |

where I1A¬ĮI^{\bar{A}}\_{1} and I2A¬ĮI^{\bar{A}}\_{2} denote the first and the second components of IA¬ĮI^{\bar{A}}.
Note that őĒ‚ÄčY0=‚ąíő≥0‚ÄčőĒ‚ÄčX0\Delta Y\_{0}=-\gamma\_{0}\Delta X\_{0} and that ő≥‚ÄčI2A¬Į‚ąíI1A¬Į=a\gamma I^{\bar{A}}\_{2}-I^{\bar{A}}\_{1}=a. It holds that őĒ‚ÄčX0=1a0őĪ0‚Äč(I0A¬Į,őĪ0‚ÄčūĚí≥0‚ąí+I0B¬Į,őĪ0)\Delta X\_{0}=\frac{1}{a\_{0}^{\alpha\_{0}}}\left(I^{\bar{A},\alpha\_{0}}\_{0}\mathcal{X}\_{0-}+I\_{0}^{\bar{B},\alpha\_{0}}\right).
‚ąé

## 5 Conclusion

In this paper, we study a class of infinite‚ÄĎhorizon stochastic control problems with regime switching arising from optimal liquidation with semimartingale strategies. We characterize the value function and the optimal strategy through three systems of BSDEs defined on an infinite time horizon. Existence of solutions to these BSDE systems is established through the development of new analytical techniques involving BMO analysis and comparison principles for multidimensional BSDEs.
The analysis of the stochastic control problem proceeds in two steps. First, we establish the well‚ÄĎposedness of the control problem by rewriting the cost functional with the aid of the BSDE characterization. Second, under additional assumptions, we prove the existence of an optimal control.

## Appendix A Results on AA.

By extending the proof in [[14](#bib.bib14), Theorem 4.2], we obtain the following wellposedness result for A¬Į\bar{A}.

###### Proposition A.1.

The system of infinite-horizon BSDEs ([2.4](#S2.E4 "In 2 Candidate BSDE systems ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies")) admits a solution (A¬Į,ZA¬Į)(\bar{A},Z^{\bar{A}}) in L‚ąě,0√óHB‚ÄčM‚ÄčO2,KA¬ĮL^{\infty,0}\times H^{2,K\_{\bar{A}}}\_{BMO} for each KA¬Į>0K\_{\bar{A}}>0. Moreover, A¬Įi\bar{A}^{i} is valued in [0,1/2][0,1/2] for each i‚ąą‚Ą≥i\in\mathcal{M}.

###### Corollary A.2.

Recall aia^{i} is defined in ([2.6](#S2.E6 "In 2 Candidate BSDE systems ‚Ä£ Stochastic Control Problems with Infinite Horizon and Regime Switching Arising in Optimal Liquidation with Semimartingale Strategies")). It satisfies 0<ŌĶ‚Č§aiő≥‚Č§c0<\epsilon\leq\frac{a^{i}}{\gamma}\leq c.
